Obstructing Japan's Aggression Against China: Refusing to Cooperate with the United States: British Policy Forged a Great Mistake: Stirrings in London Political Circles After the Publication of Stimson's New Book

(London) Today, a newspaper's book review column carried a critique of the recently published book "The Crisis in the Far East" by former U.S. Secretary of State Stimson, saying, "The materials in the book all contain dates, and the official documents are all recorded from the original text, and written in rigorous language. It is the sharpest criticism ever made by a friendly foreign minister against British foreign policy." The New Statesman and Nation magazine said, "The United Kingdom's failure to cooperate with the United States to resist Japanese aggression is one of the greatest failures in the history of the League of Nations." The inclination of most critics is to blame the United Kingdom for its failure to support President Hoover and Secretary of State Stimson's policy of refusing to recognize Japan's territorial acquisitions in China as a mistake. When the September 18th and January 28th incidents occurred, Stimson was the Secretary of State under President Hoover. In his book, Stimson sincerely evaluated British foreign policy at the time from the American perspective, which has now caused a shock in diplomatic and political circles. A surprising feature of Stimson's book is his vigorous effort to promote cooperation between the United Kingdom and the United States to implement an active policy in China, which ultimately failed. It is said that he spoke with Sir Simon (then British Foreign Secretary) three times on the transatlantic telephone, earnestly informing him that Japan's actions would endanger the world's peace system and that international cooperation should be urgently used to prevent the success of Japan's policy. Stimson said, "Based on the attitude of Sir Simon, I finally realized that the British government did not want to participate in this action, so I stopped urging them." Stimson also said that he wisely proposed invoking the Nine-Power Treaty to resist Japan, believing that the power of the City of London was the obstacle to British action. The United States was not only willing to cooperate with the League of Nations at that time, but also willing to lead other countries in carrying out everything. The fact that the member states of the League of Nations eventually accepted the principle of not recognizing the territory occupied by aggression in Geneva was still the result of the United States' vigorous advocacy. Stimson spoke highly of the value of Britain's subsequent cooperation. (Reuters dispatch on the 22nd)

French Cash Flows to the United States: Franc Devaluation May Be Inevitable

(New York) The Federal Reserve Bank of New York announced today that the value of gold shipped from France to the United States last week totaled $30,642,000. The continued inflow of European gold has caused great concern in financial circles. People here predict that the gold reserves in the upcoming reports of the Bank of France will decrease to the lowest amount since 1931, but the gold reserves of the United States are increasing every week, and will soon create a new record. Investors are quite wary in view of this fact, because the inflow of French gold proves the instability of the country's political situation and the instability of workers. Most well-informed observers here believe that the devaluation of the franc will eventually be inevitable. (Guomin dispatch on the 20th)

Western Rebel Army Advances Rapidly: Madrid in Imminent Danger: Government Troops Actively Deploy Defenses: Prepare for a Final Decisive Battle

Gibraltar: According to a telegram received here, it has been confirmed that the Spanish rebel army is approaching Madrid, and the government's position is in imminent danger. (Guomin dispatch on the 20th)

Lisbon: In view of the rapid advance of the rebel army towards Madrid, the Spanish government is now actively consolidating the defense of the capital. According to the military correspondent of the Lisbon Daily News, solid defensive works have been built around the capital, and the latest type of trench line has been constructed. The underground defenses are also very thorough. However, the work of protecting the artillery has not been completed, so the artillery is vulnerable to bombing. The fiercest battles seem to be within the city, because the People's Front is skilled in street fighting. Therefore, before the rebel army claims to be able to defeat Madrid, the city will inevitably be devastated. The buildings in all important locations in the city have been converted into forts, with a large amount of food and ammunition stored inside. Therefore, even if the rebel army breaks through the artillery forts in the suburbs, it will still take several weeks of hard fighting to occupy the entire city. (Reuters dispatch on the 21st)

Lisbon: The rebel army on the Talavera side in Spain fought fiercely with the government army all day today and is now advancing towards Madrid. According to an announcement from the rebel army, they killed 2,500 government soldiers and captured many prisoners. However, the rebel army did not state the number of casualties. It also said that the government army has no fighting spirit, and the situation of their retreat is very chaotic, abandoning many guns and ammunition. If the rebel army's claims are true, then the rebel army is currently less than 35 miles from the capital, indicating that the situation in the capital is very critical. According to a telegram from an Associated Press reporter, the rebel army on the northern front is now less than 30 miles from Madrid and can attack at any time. General Mola, commander of the rebel army on the northern front, issued a final warning to the authorities in Bilbao, demanding that the government army surrender, otherwise he will launch a bombing campaign. (Guomin dispatch on the 21st)

Siege of the Ancient Castle: Continued Hard Fighting

Madrid: The government army, which has been besieging the Moroccan-style ancient castle of Alcázar in Toledo for nine weeks, made further progress after a day of hard fighting. At the same time, a column of rebel army fighting to aid the defenders in the castle is reported to be still 14 miles away from Toledo. The government army and civilians tried to climb the walls of the castle with ladders, throwing hand grenades as they advanced, but were driven back by the rebel army's volleys. Then they bombarded the castle with artillery shells, bombs, and hand grenades for two hours, causing thick smoke and flying sand. As a result, the government army was able to occupy some locations. Spanish Prime Minister Caballero personally visited the battlefield. At the same time, the Chilean Ambassador to Spain, Mochado, is making efforts to rescue the women and children in the castle, but success is still uncertain. (Reuters dispatch on the 21st)

Toledo: Special dispatch from our reporter. The government army is intensifying its siege of the rebel army in the Alcázar Palace. In addition to using bombs and 155mm cannons and 75mm field guns to bombard the palace, they are also using aircraft to bomb it. The remaining parts of the palace have all collapsed, and the road in the palace leading to the Governor's Office (also in the hands of the rebel army) has also been cut off. Three rebel army aircraft flew over the palace yesterday to drop food to supply the defenders in the palace. They were driven away by government army aircraft. In addition, Prime Minister Caballero came here from the capital yesterday to inspect the positions and held talks with General Asensio, commander of the government army. (Havas dispatch on the 21st)

Incident of Conflict Between Chinese and Japanese Troops in Fengtai: The Goal of Forcing the 29th Army to Withdraw Has Been Achieved. The Situation in Tianjin is Tense, with Large-Scale Parades by Japanese Troops

Tianjin Correspondence: On the anniversary of the "September 18th Incident," a serious incident almost occurred at Fengtai Station on the Beining Railway. Fortunately, the 29th Army endured humiliation and sought reconciliation, and the overwhelming crisis was resolved. The course of events is described as follows:

Since this spring, a regiment of the 38th Division of the 29th Army, under the command of Zhang Zizhong, has been stationed at Fengtai Station. Later, due to a conflict over the seizure of war horses between Chinese and Japanese troops, the unit was forced to withdraw under diplomatic pressure from the Japanese side. Another regiment from the 110th Brigade of the 37th Division, the 222nd Regiment under Zhang, was stationed there, with the number of personnel reduced several times compared to before. The Japanese military barracks in Fengtai were completed in July of this year, and the number of troops increased to over a thousand, changing the relative strength of the two sides. Although the 29th Army regarded the town as a key military point, under the prevailing atmosphere of harmonious diplomacy in North China, it could only carefully arrange its defenses. However, even with the number of soldiers reduced to a battalion, the Japanese side was still not satisfied and repeatedly used indirect methods of expulsion to force the unit to withdraw. For example, on the 21st of last month, a Japanese resident named Morikawa Taro broke into Zhang's military camp for no reason, resulting in a fight with the guards in which he was stabbed and injured. The dispute lasted almost a month before it was resolved through negotiations between Matsumuro and Chen Zhongfu. Before this dispute had completely passed, a conflict suddenly broke out between the two armies on the afternoon of the 18th during a drill, escalating into a shooting. Although it is not possible to conclude that this was a planned action by the Japanese side, it can be seen from the fact that the 29th Army in Fengtai was forced to withdraw under the requested conditions, and from the statements made by Matsumuro, Hashimoto, and Wachi during their visit to Song in Peiping in mid-month, that the Japanese troops stationed in Fengtai felt threatened by the 29th Army and that Chinese troops must be withdrawn to prevent incidents. The general assessment was not entirely wrong.

The conflict on the 18th involved Sun Xiangting's 5th Company of Zhang's unit of the 29th Army. At 5:40 PM, during a fall training exercise outside the railway, they encountered a company of Japanese troops stationed locally, commanded by Captain Hozumi, who were also conducting exercises in the same direction. The two groups met on a narrow road and refused to yield. Iwai, a lieutenant and squad leader under Captain Hozumi, then took the opportunity to ride his horse into Sun's company. Unable to endure this, a soldier from Sun's company struck the horse with the butt of his rifle, sparking the conflict. The Japanese soldiers considered this an insult, and Captain Hozumi immediately ordered them to form a skirmish line and surround Sun's company, intending to disarm them. Company commander Sun Xiangting stepped forward to negotiate with the Japanese troops, but was captured and held within their lines. Sun's company was enraged and took defensive measures, confronting the Japanese troops. At this time, Major Ichiki, the commander of the Japanese battalion, received a report and led all of his soldiers to the front of Zhang's camp, setting up four machine guns to prevent soldiers from Zhang's camp from providing assistance. The standoff lasted until around 7:00 PM, when Colonel Mutaguchi Renya, the commander of the 1st Infantry Regiment of the Kawabe Brigade of the Japanese troops stationed in Peiping, led a large company of soldiers and a small artillery unit on a forced march to Fengtai. Upon arriving at Daqing Village near Fengtai, they had a misunderstanding with the 6th Company of Zhang's camp and exchanged fire. For a time, nearby houses were forcibly occupied by the Japanese soldiers, who, from their elevated positions, forced Zhang's camp to surrender. When Song Zheyuan in Tianjin received the report, he immediately telephoned Feng Zhi'an, the division commander in Peiping, instructing him to quickly cooperate with Chen Zhongfu and Japanese military officials Matsumuro, Imai, and Kawabe Brigade Commander to resolve the situation and prevent a war from breaking out. At the same time, he also sent representatives to negotiate with the headquarters of the Japanese Garrison Army in North China. The Japanese side sent Staff Officer Ikeda from Tianjin, attached member Suzuki, and Staff Officers Kai and Asai, as well as Aide-de-Camp Kawada. From Peiping, the advisers Yingjing and Nakajima (military advisers to the 29th Army) were sent. Song sent Zhen Mingzhang, a consultant to the Tianjin Municipal Government, Liu Shaokun, an advisor, and Xu Changlin, the deputy division commander of the 37th Division, among others. They set off from Peiping and Tianjin separately and met at Fengtai Station around 6:00 AM on the 19th, joining Feng's division commander Zhang. Together with Japanese Army Colonel Mutaguchi, Battalion Commander Ichiki, they held joint discussions, and it was not until 9:00 AM that a decision was reached. The two sides then lifted the confrontation. Company commander Sun Xiangting was taken to the Japanese military police headquarters in Peiping, where he was released after being questioned about any other role he might have played. Zhang's battalion began its withdrawal around 2:00 PM on the 19th and was expected to be completed by the morning of the 20th. When this incident occurred, the Tianjin Japanese military department held an emergency meeting at 11:00 PM, chaired by Tashiro, with Hashimoto and other staff members participating. The resolutions were quite serious. On the morning of the 19th, over a thousand Japanese troops stationed in Dongjuzi marched fully armed through the Dongma Road area of the city. More than ten armored vehicles also patrolled the Chinese streets in the afternoon. At 11:00 AM, staff officer Wachi was sent to visit Song Zheyuan at his private residence, conveying a serious verbal protest and demanding all rights to protect the case. For a time, people were panicked and uneasy. The Public Security Bureau's security team and armored troops were dispatched to patrol and guard the streets. In the afternoon, Cheng Jiaxian, the director of the Public Security Bureau, convened an emergency security meeting, strictly instructing the heads of each branch bureau and security team to carefully deploy their defenses. In the evening, the news of a peaceful resolution was released, and the Japanese troops also ended their demonstration parade, gradually calming the people's hearts. (19th)

Details of the Shooting of a Japanese Policeman in the Hankou Concession: Japanese Navy Lands, Police Increase Patrols, and Electric Nets Are Extensively Deployed. The Result of the Chinese-Japanese Joint Trial of Arrested Chinese Reveals No Clues

Hankou Correspondence: Yesterday (the 19th), a sudden shooting of a patrolman occurred in the Japanese Concession of Hankou. As a result, the Japanese Navy landed, police increased patrols, and a network of electric nets was extensively deployed. Many Chinese were arrested. The results of the Chinese-Japanese joint trial have so far revealed no clues. The details of what happened after the incident are recorded below. At 11:30 AM on the 19th, a patrolman at the 4th Station on Taisho Street in the Japanese Concession arrived to take over his shift and discovered that the patrolman on duty, Niichiro Yoshioka, had been shot and killed. Two bullet casings were found beside the body. The incident was reported to the head of the Japanese police station, Shimoda, who ordered all Japanese police to mobilize and be on alert. On the one hand, they searched pedestrians entering and leaving the Japanese Concession, and on the other hand, they transferred Yoshioka's body to the Doujin Hospital, where it was dissected by the head of the surgery department, Nozawa. The examination revealed that the bullet had entered from behind the left ear and through the left neck, directly penetrating the medulla oblongata, resulting in immediate death. At this time, several hundred marines from a Japanese warship landed to assist the police in enforcing martial law. The Japanese Concession suddenly entered a state of emergency. Seven Chinese were arrested: two each of peddlers and boatmen, and three small vendors. They were all detained at the Japanese police station for questioning. Fortunately, the boatmen and pedestrians were released, while the vendors were detained for trial. After receiving notification from the Japanese side, Wu Guozhen, the mayor of Hankou, expressed his condolences to the Japanese Consul General Miura by telephone. Chen Xizeng, the director of the Public Security Bureau, also sent Inspector Wang Yufen, Section Chief Dong Keren, and Wan Dixiu, the director of the 13th Branch Bureau of Public Security, to the Japanese police station to express their condolences to Shimoda, the head of the station, and stated that if the Japanese side needed assistance from the Chinese authorities in the investigation or arrest of the murderer, the Chinese authorities would provide assistance. The Japanese side expressed its gratitude for this. While the Japanese police continued to search pedestrians, the naval marines had already returned to their ships, and order gradually returned to normal. At night, the Japanese marines landed again and formed patrol teams of four men each, patrolling throughout the night. On the morning of the 20th, the Japanese police doubled the number of patrolmen and intensified the inspection of pedestrians. Electric nets were also set up at the entrances of various roads, and the situation became even more tense than before. In the afternoon, the Japanese side requested that the Chinese authorities send personnel to jointly try the captured vendors. The municipal government sent Secretary Zhang Jinghuai, the Public Security Bureau sent Inspector Wang Yufen and Section Chief Dong Keren to the Japanese police station to conduct a joint trial with the Japanese police officers. However, among the captured vendors, one was an elderly man named Huang Qingyun, who was 73 years old, and another was a child named Liu Xiya, who was only eight years old. Huang lived at No. 40, Third Lane, Lower Slope, and Liu lived at No. 22, Yongqing Street. Both made a living selling cigarettes and sundries. One was senile, and the other was ignorant, so the results of the interrogation revealed no clues. On that evening, the security in the Japanese Concession was tightened. Five Japanese warships, including the Ataka, Katata, Futami, and Ren, were anchored on the river. Commander Hino, stationed on the Ataka, also landed to meet with Consul Miura and military officials to hold discussions. At the same time, Japanese residents held a general meeting at the Kojikai Club to exchange views on the case. Takamichi Kazuo, dispatched by the Japanese residents in Shanghai, and Hikita Tetsutaro, dispatched by the Japanese residents in Beijing, arrived in Hankou by China Aviation airplane to conduct investigations. After the incident occurred, the Japanese deputy chief, Shirai, issued a statement, stating on the one hand that the location of the incident was not under the jurisdiction of the Japanese Concession, and on the other hand that when the deceased was shot, he was buying cigarettes at a cigarette stall, so bullet casings were left near the cigarette stall, and that the discovery of his body near the post was probably because the Chinese in the vicinity moved the body to the post after the incident. This is far from the truth. The location where Yoshioka was killed was at the Taisho Street intersection in the Japanese Concession, 300 meters from the post of the 13th Branch Police Station of the Chinese authorities. A post had already been set up between them, but in August of the 17th year of the Republic of China, Ogawa, the head of the Japanese Police Station, notified the 4th Public Security Bureau and ordered the post to be removed and prohibited from being set up. The Taisho Street intersection is even more within the scope of the Japanese Concession. As for the bullet casings found, they are indeed worth investigating. The type of bullet is the smallest "Berliner." This gun cannot hit a person unless it is extremely close, and the Chinese never use this type of bullet. If the Japanese authorities pay attention to this, the facts of the case may become clear. (20th)

The General Assembly of the Jiangsu Provincial Chamber of Commerce Held Its First and Second General Assemblies Yesterday: Requesting a Temporary Suspension of Income Tax Collection to Relieve Commercial Distress; Housing Donations Must Be Implemented After Local Consent

Zhenjiang Correspondence: The Jiangsu Provincial Chamber of Commerce began holding its 5th Member General Assembly on the 20th. The opening ceremony was held in the morning, and the proposal review meeting was held in the afternoon, divided into four groups: Donation and Tax Group, Regulations Group, Financial Relief Group, and General Affairs Group. The review was gradually completed by the evening. The First Assembly was held yesterday morning at 10:00 AM.

First Assembly

Chaired by Yu Xiaochuan, after the report, discussions began. (1) Draft budget for the association for the 25th year. It was resolved to submit it to the conveners of the four group proposal review committees and one person appointed by the presidium for joint review. (2) The association's financial statement for the 24th year and the statement of expenditures for the 24th year were resolved to be reviewed together with the previous proposal reviewers. Discussions then began on the proposals from each group.

Donation and Tax Group

(1) Request for exemption from slaughter and business taxes. It was resolved to submit a request to the provincial government for approval of the exemption to alleviate commercial distress. (2) Request for exemption from the business tax on silk fabrics. It was resolved to submit a request to the Ministry of Finance for amendment. (3) Request that the provincial government collect business taxes based on the actual situation of the shops and avoid increasing the extra burden. It was resolved to order the provincial government to instruct various county bureaus to quickly organize evaluation committees to collect taxes based on the actual business situation, taking into account both national taxes and commercial conditions. (4) Request to avoid increasing the business tax rate. It was resolved to submit separate requests to the Ministry of Finance, the provincial government, and the provincial finance department to continue collecting taxes according to the previously set tax rate, avoiding changes, and to entrust the next executive committee to continue striving for it. At the same time, the representatives of the presidium of the general assembly went to the provincial government to petition. (5) The province's independently implemented shop and housing donation exceeds the scope of reorganizing housing donations, which should be discussed. It was resolved to submit the entire case to the central government. The implementation of housing donations in Jiangsu Province must comply with central regulations and be implemented after the consent of local groups in Jiangsu Province. Discussions on the proposals ended here, and the meeting adjourned after 12:00 noon.

Second Assembly

Held at 3:00 PM. Chaired by Lan Bohua, after performing the rituals, discussions continued on the proposals from the Donation and Tax Group. (6) Request to reduce the brokerage tax in Yancheng. (Resolution:) Send separate letters to the provincial government to handle the Yancheng brokerage tax in accordance with the practices of other counties in northern Jiangsu. (7) Request that the Ministry of Finance stipulate standards for collecting income tax. (Resolution:) Refer to the executive committee for consideration and handling. (8) Request for a postponement of income tax collection to alleviate commercial distress. (Resolution:) The general assembly will submit a request to the national government to postpone the implementation until various miscellaneous donations have been abolished. (9) The Chongming Business Tax Bureau's brokerage tax collection office illegally extorts cotton farmers and small vendors' business tax on cotton. (Resolution:) Submit to the provincial government for prompt and effective prevention. (10) The disparity in tobacco and alcohol license taxes between the Ding and Wu levels should be amended. (Resolution:) Forwarded to the central government. (11) Request to correct the Jiangsu Provincial Education Fund Management Office's illegal collection of brokerage tax. (Resolution:) The general assembly will forward a request to the provincial government to issue a clear order to exempt the timber industry and self-employed businesses from the brokerage tax. (12) Request the general assembly to request the central government to reduce the business tax rate on cotton. (The rest omitted)

Financial Group

(1) It is proposed to request the provincial government to issue a circular to the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, the Jiangsu Farmers Bank, and other banks to set up more agricultural warehouses and reduce interest rates to reduce the burden on farmers. (Resolution:) Forwarded to the provincial government. (2) Fluctuations in the market price of copper coins have a significant impact on commerce. The government should take overall measures to maintain balance. (Resolution:) Principle passed, recommending that the Ministry of Finance and the provincial government consider and implement it. (3) Many damaged legal tender and subsidiary currency notes are in circulation, requesting discussion of relief measures. (Resolution:) Suggest the Ministry of Finance to consider and implement it. (4) The Jiangsu Farmers Bank's small-loan lending program for industry and commerce should be extended to all counties in the province. (Resolution:) Submit a request to the provincial government to order the bank to earnestly implement it in order to achieve universal access. (The rest of the proposals omitted)

Regulations Group

(1) Request to suggest that the government amend the Chamber of Commerce Law and the Industry and Commerce Association Law to force businesses in the same industry to join the association and for the association to join the Chamber of Commerce. (Resolution:) Forwarded to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for adoption and implementation. (2) Request to suggest that the government amend Article 19, Paragraph 1 of the Chamber of Commerce Law to change the term of office of executive committee members and supervisors to two years, with half of them being re-elected each year and eligible for re-election. (Resolution:) Still handled in accordance with the Chamber of Commerce Law. (3) Request that the government change the procedures for punishing stamp tax violations to administrative penalties or rulings, and notify the post office for delivery in order to benefit merchants. (Resolution:) Passed. (4) Shops in the same industry with fewer than seven members should all join the Chamber of Commerce to become shop members. (Resolution:) Forwarded to the central government.

General Affairs Group

(1) Preventing smuggling: The situation in Songjiang is special, and the provincial government should be requested to strictly maintain defense to prevent economic aggression. (Resolution:) Chambers of commerce in various counties should quickly organize private inspection sub-committees to handle it. (2) Poisonous soy sauce has been found on the market, which is harmful to health. It is suggested that the Ministry of Civil Affairs issue a circular to all cities and counties in the province to strictly prohibit it. (Resolution:) Passed. (3) Restore the Chamber of Commerce to maintain the market. (Resolution:) Reserved. (4) Cases of ancestral guarantee lawsuits in shops or proof of various matters must have a specified shop chop method effective. (Resolution:) Handed over to the next executive committee. (5) The Tariff Inspection Office of Hebei and Chahar collects private goods tax rates that harm national sovereignty and hinder industry. (Resolution:) Request the Ministry of Finance to promptly stop it. (6) It is suggested that the government should promote the establishment of more factories to utilize agricultural products from northern Jiangsu to benefit the people's livelihood. (Resolution:) Handed over to the next executive committee to draft measures to submit to the provincial government for handling.

Temporary Motions

(1) It is proposed to request exemption from the cotton improvement fee in northern Jiangsu. (Resolution:) Passed. (2) Zhejiang Province plunders the only fishing area in the Jiangsu sea area, the Shengsi Islands, which has a huge impact on the fishing industry economy of Jiangsu Province. Send a telegram in the name of the General Assembly to the central finance department to strive for it. (Resolution:) Passed. The meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM.

Recent Situation in Guangdong and Guangxi (2)

— Our Reporter Xiao An

Chairman Huang's Remarks

Huang Musong, the chairman of the Guangdong Provincial Government, is a senior figure in the Guangdong military. The Fourth Army Commander Yu Hanmou and others are all his students. Huang used to be the superintendent of the Whampoa Military Academy, training many military talents. Huang has been a member of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission in recent years and has always been relied upon by the central government. Last month, Yu Hanmou went to Beijing to attend the Second Plenary Session and asked the central government to lead his troops back to Guangdong from southern Jiangxi. Huang and Yu had a teacher-student relationship, so Huang's support for Yu in Beijing was quite effective. Therefore, the Guangdong situation was settled, and Huang was ordered to preside over the provincial government. Huang is humble and amiable, pays attention to moral integrity, and meets with guests every day to broadly collect public opinion, which is a great blessing for Guangdong Province.

The reporter went to the provincial government at 4:30 PM on the 18th to see Huang. At that time, Li Zongren and Huang Xuchu also came to the provincial government to pay a visit to Huang. After Li and Huang bid farewell, Huang met with the reporter in the chairman's office. Huang inquired about the situation of the newspaper. The reporter expressed his respect for the Guangdong provincial government's decision to implement a ban on gambling and abolish exorbitant and miscellaneous taxes. Huang then talked about how the provincial government's annual shortfalls of more than 14 million yuan after the gambling ban made administrative expenses difficult. Subsidies for educational undertakings and other facilities in various counties and districts also largely depended on the additional gambling revenue. After the gambling ban, the additional fees were also abolished, so the future of educational undertakings and other facilities in various counties and districts was naturally also affected. However, banning gambling and abolishing exorbitant taxes were to eliminate harm for the people and to remove past malpractices, so the government resolutely implemented them without any worries, etc. The reporter then asked about the new government's future administrative policies. Huang then spoke at length about the necessity of political construction and educational construction, saying that in the past few years, Chen Bonan's three-year plan, whether good or bad, focused on material construction and industrial construction. However, material construction and industrial construction are not the most urgent needs at present. If we can first start with political construction, making politics on track, officials honest, and the people happy in their work, and at the same time strive for educational construction to improve national knowledge and enable them to distinguish between benefits and harms, then material construction and industrial construction will be easier to promote and achieve success. As for those in power, the heavier the responsibility, the stricter they should be in restraining themselves, and they must use the highest moral character as an example for their subordinates. Only those who can be admired by the people can achieve good results in governance. By the time the conversation reached this point, more than 20 minutes had passed, and the reporter then made his farewells.

Songjiang: Arrest of Refugees for Robbery

Yesterday (the 20th), 137 refugees, men, women, children, and elderly, from Ruanjiang County, Hunan Province, suddenly arrived in Xinqiao Town, a part of the county. Led by Xu Junwei and Wang Dimin as representatives, they went directly to the town's patrol station to present their passports upon arrival. The refugees were then divided into groups and sent to various villages to beg for food. About 50 or 60 refugees also came to Panlong Township and crowded into Lu Qintang's house to demand food. They then went to the house of his brother, Lu Yonggen. Yonggen's daughter, Fengzhen, was about to be married and was rushing to prepare her wedding clothes and purchase gold and silver jewelry. The refugees, taking advantage of their numbers, robbed all the clothes and jewelry and also injured Lu Qintang's head in the resistance, causing a wound and profuse bleeding. Villagers, seeing this, hurriedly beat gongs to gather a crowd, detained the refugee representatives Xu and Wang, and the rest scattered and fled. The villagers then tied up the refugee representatives and sent them to the Sixth Sub-Station of Sijing, who transferred them to the main bureau. Bureau Chief He Runzhang, considering that the refugees were causing disturbances in the countryside and urgently needed to be suppressed, immediately dispatched Detective Yang Shijie and Inspector Yang Jingjiang to Sijing to investigate and interrogate the refugee representatives. They all denied leading the crowd in robbery, and the victim, Lu Qintang, also feared making enemies and was unwilling to pursue the matter, saying that he would seek medical treatment for his injuries himself. The autumn harvest is coming in the four rural districts and the refugees will continue to pour in. The public safety in the villages is worth noting.

Suzhou: Adulterous Woman Elopes with Thief

Hui Fubei, a resident of Beizhuang, part of Nanqiao Town in Suzhou, used to work in a dyeing factory in Shanghai. Recently, he has been unemployed and makes a living by farming at home. When Fubei was in Shanghai, his wife, Wang, became intimate with Liu Jinbao. Now that Fubei is at home, the adulterous couple cannot act as they please, so they came up with a strange idea. Wang colluded with Liu, who invited more than ten hooligans, each carrying a weapon. At about 4 a.m. the day before yesterday (the 20th), they crowded into Cao's house to rob. Wang acted as an inside accomplice, tying up Cao Fubei and others, and also injuring Cao's father, Yinbao (who is over eighty years old). They looted for three hours before Liu and Yu Dou took Wang away along with the stolen goods and fled together. Yesterday, Cao Fubei reported the case to the Public Security Bureau for investigation.

Arrest of Traffickers

Yesterday (the 21st) at about 2 p.m., Patrol Officer Liang Biwu of the 32nd Sub-Station, acting on a tip, learned that there was human trafficking activity at No. 118 Dongfang Hotel in the North Bureau. He immediately led police officers to arrest Zhang Daogen and his daughter Da Yuan (20 years old), who lived at No. 161 Wuqufang, as well as Zhu Peigen and his wife, Ye, and a woman named Zhou Jin, who lived in Duan'anli, Xinzha Road, Shanghai. All of them were taken to the station and sent to the bureau for interrogation.

Wuxi: Female Student Commits Suicide by Jumping into a Well

Pan Liying, a 17-year-old first-year student at Shuxue Girls' Middle School in Yingshanhe, Guangfu Gate, was from Bijie County, Guizhou Province. Since childhood, she had been betrothed to Wang Mingzhong, a fellow villager, through her parents' arrangement. Mingzhong is now 16 years old and not yet married. His uncle, Wang Puqing, is currently the battalion commander of the Communications Battalion of the 36th Division of the Army, stationed in Huishan in this city. During the summer vacation, Mingzhong, his sister Mingxiao, and his fiancée Pan Liying came south from Guizhou to study. Mingzhong was admitted to Nandou Wangnan Middle School, and Mingxiao and Liying were admitted to the first year of Shuxue Girls' Middle School in Yingshanhe. Since the start of school, it has not been two weeks. They all lived in the school. Their grades were good. On the afternoon of the 16th of this month, Liying suddenly felt dizzy after physical education class and asked for leave to rest in the dormitory upstairs. The school arranged for Dr. Xu Fenghua, the school doctor, to treat her. However, Liying was not used to taking Western medicine. The next day, she was accompanied by a servant, Zhao Ma, to see the Chinese medicine doctor Deng Xingbo, who diagnosed her with malaria. She took the decoction, and by the 19th, the chills and fever had subsided, and she went to class as usual. On the 20th (Sunday) at about 1 p.m., Liying, along with her aunt Qi Mingxiao and several classmates, went to the Huofo Photo Studio in Shengxiangkou to take pictures. At about 5 p.m., Liying returned to school alone to rest, but suddenly felt hot all over and extremely upset. At that time, her nerves seemed to be confused, and she ran outside alone. Ms. Song Shiwen, the Director of Studies of the school, and Ms. Kuang Weiwen, a teacher, went forward to chase and persuade her to return to school. When they reached the courtyard next to the third canteen, Liying, taking advantage of their unpreparedness, suddenly jumped into a well to commit suicide. Mingxiao tried to save her, only grabbing her hand, but because she was unable to hold on, she still fell. She immediately shouted for help. After being rescued by the school servant and neighbors, she was already beyond recovery. The school immediately notified the family of the deceased, Battalion Commander Wang, to come to the school to handle the funeral arrangements. It is said that Liying had written a suicide note, which was handed over to the First Branch of the Public Security Bureau for safekeeping. The reason for her suicide is not very clear. Yesterday (the 21st) at 9 a.m., Zheng Jintai, the chief of the local district, reported the case to the court for inspection. The appointed prosecutor went to the scene with officials for the inquest, but the family of the deceased requested to be exempted from the inquest. The prosecutor approved it and ordered them to prepare a coffin and collect the body.

Changshu: Carelessness at the Dalu Pharmacy

At about 2 a.m. this morning (the 21st), the Dalu Pharmacy on Siqian Street here was suddenly destroyed by a fire due to negligence, resulting in the death of an apprentice and a loss of more than 10,000 yuan. According to the investigation, the cause of the fire was that a shop runner from Shanghai introduced an apprentice named Bao Haopei from Shaoxing, Zhejiang Province, to the store on the afternoon of the 20th. After being introduced through various connections, he was able to come to Changshu on the afternoon of the 20th. However, it is customary for stores in the interior to light large red candles for the apprentice to pay respects to the master when they first enter the store. Although the apprentice Bao was from out of town, he could not be an exception. Unexpectedly, the candle was not completely burned by midnight. At about 1 a.m., the shopkeepers had already fallen asleep. The candle suddenly toppled over, causing other items to catch fire and leading to the conflagration. When the fire was raging, the other shopkeepers all jumped down from the upper floor and ran away, but the newly arrived apprentice Bao was unfamiliar with the path and was even more panicked after the incident, unable to escape, and thus perished in the fire. It was truly tragic. It is reported that the owner of the pharmacy, Gu Yulin, started by peddling Japanese goods and has now accumulated tens of thousands of yuan to set up this relatively well-equipped Dalu Pharmacy. Now that it has been destroyed, the total loss is estimated to be over 10,000 yuan, although it was insured for 3,000 taels, it is still far from enough.

The Final Payment of Principal and Interest on the Jiangzhe Silk Industry Short-Term Public Bonds Will Be Paid by the Six Banks at the End of the Month

The total amount of the Jiangzhe Silk Industry Short-Term Public Bonds issued in 1932 was three million yuan. The Fund Management Committee, in accordance with the regulations, held a lottery every three months to repay the principal and pay interest. As for the sixteenth and final payment of principal and interest, it is approved to be paid at the end of September. Because it is the final payment, there is no need for another lottery. Here is the announcement: "The sixteenth and final payment of principal and interest on this public bond will begin on the 30th of this month. All those holding unredeemed bonds with the numbers 'No. 01,' 'No. 05,' 'No. 21,' 'No. 47,' 'No. 54,' 'No. 92,' 'No. 97,' and 'No. 7' are requested to present their tickets to the six banks—Central, China, Communications, Guohuo, Jiangsu, and Hangzhou Zhejiang Local—to redeem them for national currency. Those who have won the lottery in previous rounds but have not yet received the payment are also requested to present their tickets to the above-mentioned six banks to receive the principal and interest as soon as possible. This is a special announcement."

Six-Percent British Gold Bonds: Bond Certificates Are About to be Printed; The Railway Department Will Exchange Preliminary Certificates

In order to complete the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway, the Railway Department entered into a contract with the Sino-British Banking Corporation and the China Construction Banking Corporation to establish a six-percent British gold loan and formally issue 1.1 million pounds of "Six-Percent British Gold Bonds for the Completion of the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway in 1936" on the 16th of this month, with an annual interest rate of six percent, paid every six months, and the principal to be repaid after five years. The Central, China, Communications, and HSBC banks were entrusted to act as agents for the fund-raising, and the full amount was subscribed on June 17. According to a reporter, the bond certificates are divided into two types, 50 pounds and 100 pounds in British gold. Those purchased by Chinese and British people at that time were preliminary certificates. Since the formal certificates have been actively printed by the Commercial Press, they will be delivered soon. At that time, the Railway Department will officially announce that bondholders will exchange for the formal bond certificates.

Regarding the Shanghai-Guangdong long-distance telephone, at 7 a.m. on the 21st, the Liu Hang Radio Station first communicated with Guangdong, and Guangdong responded immediately. German Ambassador to China, Doddmann, will Arrive in Shanghai in Early November

Since German Ambassador to China, Mr. Doddmann, left China with his wife in June to return to Germany for vacation and report to the German Ministry of Foreign Affairs, several months have passed. All of Doddmann's tasks have been completed. According to a reporter from Shen Shi News Agency who learned from the German Consulate in this port, Doddmann was originally scheduled to leave Germany and return to China in early November. He is now ordered to shorten his vacation and return to China in advance. Therefore, Doddmann left Germany by transport ship today (21st) and will travel to China via the United States. When the transport ship arrives in the United States, Doddmann will disembark for a short stay, and then depart from the United States for Shanghai, which is expected to arrive on November 5th.

The Municipal Party Department Convened the Zhu Zhixin Martyrdom Memorial Meeting Yesterday; Jiang Huaisu Reported the Significance of the Memorial; The Whole City Lowered Flags to Half-Mast, and the Chinese Concession was on Alert

Yesterday (21st) was the anniversary of Mr. Zhu Zhixin's martyrdom. The Municipal Party Department specially convened representatives from all walks of life at 10 a.m. yesterday in the assembly hall of the department to hold a memorial meeting. The chairman was Jiang Huaisu, the recorder was Du Mengsen, and the master of ceremonies was Zhang Hanyun. The whole city uniformly lowered flags to half-mast in mourning, and the Chinese Concession authorities were on high alert. The details are as follows:

Meeting Place Arrangement

The meeting place was the assembly hall of the Municipal Party Department. The party and national flags and a white cloth banner were hung in front of the gate, with the words "Shanghai Municipal Representatives from All Walks of Life Hold the Sixteenth Anniversary Memorial Meeting of Mr. Zhu Zhixin's Martyrdom." The party and national flags and the portrait of the Premier were hung in the center of the hall. Order slogans were posted on the left and right, and slogans were pasted all over the four walls. The arrangement was quite solemn.

Attending Representatives

Jiang Huaisu from the Municipal Party Department, Huang Kegui from the Municipal Education Association, Lin Kecong from the Municipal Women's Association, Wang Xuequan from the China Education Association, Huang Xianggu from the Chinese Residents Association in the French Concession, Mao Yun from the Second Special District Citizens' Association, Feng Jianhua from the Military Training Association, Zhu Dongwen from the Civic Training Office, He Yuanming from the Accountants' Association, Du Mengsen from the Cooperative Enterprise Promotion Association, Zhu Shide from the National Goods Maintenance Association, Li Huaixiong from the Youth Lecture Group, Zhao Zhenhui from the Pharmaceutical Workers' Union, and more than 200 representatives from various agencies, organizations, large, medium, and small schools, district party departments, and district branches.

Meeting Order

(1) Opening of the meeting, (2) Singing of the party song, (5) Bowing three times to the party and national flags and the portrait of the Premier, (4) Reading the Premier's last will and testament, (5) Three minutes of silence to mourn the martyr Mr. Zhu Zhixin, (6) Reporting, (7) Speech, (8) Calling slogans, (9) Adjournment.

Chairman's Report

After the rituals, the chairman reported, saying that today is the memorial week and is combined with the memorial meeting for Mr. Zhu Zhixin's martyrdom. Sixteen years ago today was the day of Mr. Zhu's martyrdom. At that time, Lu Rongting and Cao Rongxin occupied Guangzhou, and the people were in dire straits. Mr. Zhu feared that the revolutionary forces would be interrupted, so he followed the Premier's order to contact the army to suppress Mo, occupied the Humen Fort, and was unfortunately assassinated by the Guixi rebels. He was only thirty-six years old. Mr. Zhu was thrifty, diligent in his studies, and always had a book in his hand. He was a model for future generations. His revolutionary achievements are even more indelible. The current situation is more dangerous than when Mr. Zhu was martyred. Incidents in Chengdu, Beihai, Hankou, and Fengtai have occurred one after another. Although the Fengtai incident has now come to an end, we can only strive for survival in this environment. Now our country only fears internal troubles and does not worry about external conflicts. The recent Guangdong-Guangxi incident has been peacefully resolved, and it has had a good impact on all other incidents. This matter is entirely due to Mr. Jiang's magnanimity and appropriate measures. Otherwise, international incidents would definitely worsen. Today, in commemorating Mr. Zhu, we must emulate Mr. Zhu's thrift and diligence in learning, and at the same time, we should admire Mr. Jiang's spirit of hard work. Everyone should work hard to survive and strive forward. Then he called slogans, and the ceremony was adjourned.

Meeting Slogans

(1) Inherit the spirit of Mr. Zhu, (2) Emulate the personality of Mr. Zhu, (3) The spirit of Mr. Zhu Zhixin is immortal, (4) Long live the Chinese Kuomintang, (5) Long live the Republic of China.

Half-Mast Alert

Yesterday, the Municipal Party Department convened the memorial meeting for Mr. Zhu Zhixin's martyrdom. All organs, organizations, large, medium, and small schools, and all levels of party departments in this city, in addition to sending representatives to participate in the memorial meeting, also lowered flags to half-mast for one day in mourning. The Municipal Public Security Bureau and the police departments of the two concessions, considering yesterday to be a revolutionary memorial day and fearing that unscrupulous elements would take advantage of the opportunity to cause trouble, ordered their subordinates to implement vigilance.

Baoshan Seawall: Leaks Urgently Need Major Repairs; Dangerous Sections Destroyed by Hurricanes are Repaired; The Construction Bureau Has Sent Personnel for Inspection and Returned to the Province to Report

The Baoshan County seawall was breached during the recent hurricane. The breached embankment in Beishidong has now been repaired. The Construction Bureau of Jiangsu Province believes that the autumn flood season is approaching and the safety of the seawall is of great importance. It has sent engineers to inspect it for repairs. The details are as follows:

Dangerous Sections in Beishidong Completed

The Baoshan County seawall is located at a strategic point of the river and sea and is the most important area for seawall construction in Jiangnan. During each autumn season, the seawall is often eroded by the sea waves. During the recent hurricane, the embankment in Beishidong was completely destroyed by the strong winds and waves. Zhang Mingjing, the magistrate of the county, in addition to reporting to the provincial bureau, instructed the seawall construction office to rush to repair it day and night. The damaged embankments have been blocked with mud and burlap bags, and wooden piles have been driven around the body of the seawall. The dangerous sections have now been completed, and temporary emergency repair materials have been set up to prevent accidents.

The Entire Seawall Project Urgently Needs Major Repairs

The county's seawall is connected to Shanghai and the counties of Taicang and Liuhe. The east and west seawalls, such as Xiaosabei, Beiwangmiao, Wuyuedun, Beishidong, Chenhuabin, and other places, are all at the confluence of the Yangtze River and the Yellow Sea, and the tides are particularly strong. The autumn winds and waves are even more violent. However, due to funding reasons, the entire seawall project has only been repaired temporarily for several years. The body of each section of the seawall is full of leaks, and there are many dangers. The Mid-Autumn Festival flood season is approaching, and the situation is extremely dangerous. Therefore, the people of the county all hope that the province will allocate funds for repairs so that the seawall can be permanently safe.

The Construction Bureau Pays Attention and Sends Personnel for Inspection

After receiving the county government's report, the Jiangsu Provincial Construction Bureau paid great attention to the issue of seawall safety as the autumn flood was approaching. It sent Engineer Tu to inspect it. He was very satisfied with the temporary emergency repair project built by the county. If there are no excessive winds and waves during the autumn flood season, there is nothing to worry about. However, the decision to repair the entire seawall project must be made by the provincial authorities. The engineer has completed the inspection and returned to the province to report.

Long-Distance Telephone: Cancellation Procedure; The Ministry of Communications Has Revised it; Pilot Program in Beijing-Hankou and Shanghai-Hankou

In order to facilitate the public and promote business, the Ministry of Communications has ruled that when using long-distance telephones between Beijing and Hankou or Shanghai and Hankou, if the caller only knows the name and address of the called party and does not know their telephone number, they may also apply for registration. If the reported called party is found not to have a telephone installed, or if the installed telephone has been renamed or transferred, or if their name does not match the one listed in the telephone directory and cannot be found, resulting in the inability to connect, a free cancellation of the registration will be allowed. Regarding the advance notice, when registering a telephone call, the caller may simultaneously apply to the calling station to notify the called party, "If the specified called party is not present, resulting in the inability to speak, the telegraph office will notify the called party to inform the calling party that they wish to call back at a certain time." The calling station should notify the receiving station and then notify the called party to follow up. It is reported that the above two new measures have been ordered by the Ministry of Communications to be piloted by the telephone bureaus in the capital, Wuhan, and Shanghai from October 1.

Tao Baichuan Will Arrive in Shanghai Today

Tao Baichuan, a member of the executive committee of the Municipal Party Department of this city, left the country last year and has been away for almost a year. The Municipal Party Department has telegraphed Mr. Tao to return to the country early. Mr. Tao left Europe last month and returned to the country by special trip. Special Trip Back to the Country

Mr. Tao left the country last year and went to Harvard University Graduate School in the United States, specializing in political science. In addition to his studies, he also engaged in writing. All of his writings are often published in various newspapers and magazines at home and abroad. In July of this year, Mr. Tao took the French mail ship Normandy from the United States to Europe. First he went to England, then to the Soviet Union, and then to Finland, Norway, Sweden, Denmark, Germany, France, Italy, and other countries. He traveled and inspected the political situation in each country. During his travels, Mr. Tao once entered the University of London to continue studying political science. Later, due to repeated telegrams from the Municipal Party Department of this city, he left Europe in the middle of last month and returned to the country by special trip.

Arriving in Shanghai This Morning

The French mail ship Asia Tena, on which Mr. Tao is traveling, will arrive in Shanghai at seven o'clock this morning and will dock at the China Merchants Bureau Central Wharf on Broadway Road. The various agencies and groups in this city believe that Mr. Tao has been warmly received by celebrities from all walks of life in Europe and the United States, so they have prepared to welcome him on his triumphant return. Representatives from various agencies and groups and Mr. Tao's relatives and friends are all scheduled to go to the port to welcome him this morning.

Reporting to Nanjing

Mr. Tao's trip abroad was entrusted by the central government and various agencies in this city with the mission of investigation and inspection. Therefore, Mr. Tao reported his findings from time to time, and after arriving in Shanghai, in addition to visiting Mayor Wu, he is scheduled to go to Nanjing to meet with the central authorities in the short term to report on the recent political construction in various countries. It is reported that Mr. Tao's books, "Party Politics" and "A Visit to the Soviet Union," will be printed and published after his return to the country.

Issuance Begins Next Month: £1.1 Million Loan Secured

Repayment from Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Revenue, Not to Be Circulated, Fully Underwritten by Syndicate

A "Shen Shi News" report: To complete the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway, the Ministry of Railways, in May of this year, concluded a £6,000,000 gold loan agreement with a syndicate formed by the Sino-British Banking Corporation and the China Construction Bank. The total amount is £1.1 million (approximately 1.8 million in national currency). After repaying the syndicate's hot money and the outstanding balance owed to the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Railway Company, the remainder will be used to complete the entire Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo line and to build the Qiantang River Bridge and the Nanxing Bridge branch line. The contract has been approved by the Executive Yuan and the Central Political Conference and submitted to the Legislative Yuan for review and approval. The loan bonds have been entrusted by the Ministry of Railways to the Commercial Press for printing and will be ready soon. The official issuance will begin on the first of next month. The face value is denominated in English gold, divided into three types: £10, £50, and £100. It is understood that in the future, it will not be circulated on the market and will be fully underwritten by the Sino-British Banking Corporation and the China Construction Bank syndicate. After the bonds are delivered, the syndicate will allocate the funds in installments according to the contract provisions. The bonds bear an annual interest rate of 6% and a term of 25 years. Only interest will be paid for the first five years, and principal will be repaid starting in the sixth year, with full repayment by the 50th year of the Republic. The Ministry of Railways has established a management committee to specifically manage the fund for principal and interest repayment, and a portion of the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway's operating revenue and the Ministry of Railways' share of the Qiantang River Bridge revenue will be allocated to the management committee as collateral for principal and interest repayment.

Page 10

Central, China, and Communications Banks Ordered to Collect

Income Tax on Government Bonds and Savings Deposits, Collection Method Adopted Reporting System, Liang Hejun and Others Visited Banking Industry Yesterday to Discuss

"Xin Xin News" reports: The Ministry of Finance has decided to levy income tax, and on the first of next month, it will first implement three types of tax revenue: civil servants' salaries, government bond interest, and bank deposits. It has also ordered the Central, China, and Communications Banks and the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau to collect the taxes. Liang Hejun, deputy director of the Direct Tax Preparation Office, and others consulted with the banking industry yesterday on the collection procedures. Details of each situation are as follows:

Three Banks Ordered to Collect Taxes

The three types of income tax to be levied starting on October 1st—civil servants' salaries, government bond interest, and bank deposits—will be handled as follows: Income tax on civil servants' salaries will be deducted and remitted by the accounting departments of the relevant government agencies according to the prescribed amounts. For the remaining income taxes, such as government bond interest and bank deposit interest, the Ministry of Finance has stipulated that they will be collected by the Central, China, and Communications Banks, as well as the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau of the Ministry of Communications. It is understood that the four institutions have received official orders from the Ministry of Finance, instructing their branches, sub-branches, and offices throughout the country to collect the taxes.

Reporting Method Adopted

The method for collecting income tax on bank deposits and government bond interest has now been decided to be a reporting system, whereby each bank and money shop is responsible for voluntarily reporting the amount of government bonds and deposits held by the bank. The Central Direct Tax Preparation Office will then investigate based on the account books reported by each bank and money shop, and the income tax will be deducted by the bank and money shop from the interest of the depositors. If there are any omissions, the bank and money shop will be responsible. After this method is implemented, bank and money shop employees will have an additional procedure, and depositors and government bondholders will have no way to evade the tax. Therefore, the collection of taxes will not be missed.

Liang Hejun Visits Banking Sector for Discussions

After Liang Hejun (respectfully marrying), deputy director of the Central Direct Tax Preparation Office of the Ministry of Finance, was dispatched to Shanghai with Ning Encheng and Qu Zhaorong, the three visited leaders of the banking and money industries in the city yesterday morning and afternoon, including Chen Xing, vice president of the Central Bank, Chen Guangfu, chairman of the Bankers Association, Lin Kanghou, secretary-general, Bei Songsun, manager of the Shanghai branch of the Bank of China, Zhang Peishen, manager of the Business Bureau of the Bank of Communications, Qin Runqing, and Pei Yunqing of the Money Industry Association. They sought opinions on the collection of income tax and discussed methods for deducting income tax on interest from government bonds and savings deposits. The results were quite satisfactory. It is said that after completing their business in Shanghai, Liang and others plan to return to Beijing today to report.

Invitations for Discussions Today and Tomorrow

A Central News Agency report states that income tax on bank deposits and government bond interest income will be levied starting on October 1st. The banking and money industries in the city have all taken note of this and are conducting separate studies. The Bankers Association believes that the handling procedures are quite complicated and require sufficient time for thorough discussion. Therefore, the association has recommended Zhang Peishen and others to visit Gao Bingfang, director of the Central Direct Tax Preparation Office, during their trip to Beijing, and also submitted a request to the Ministry of Finance to postpone implementation. According to banking sources yesterday, the Ministry of Finance believes that the implementation of income tax has been publicly announced by the National Government and cannot be changed. For the convenience of implementation, it has ordered the Direct Tax Preparation Office to send personnel to contact the banking and money industries. It is reported that Liang Hejun, deputy director of the office, and others have contacted the persons in charge of the Central, China, and Communications Banks and the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, requesting the three banks to invite the persons in charge of each bank to hold detailed discussions today and tomorrow in order to start operations on schedule. The banking industry hopes that a practical solution can be decided within one week before the start of operations, so that interest on deposits can be closed on September 30th, and there will be sufficient time to inform branches in various locations to handle the matter simultaneously. The taxes to be collected will be deducted and reported by each bank, and the tax collection office will send personnel to supervise at any time. It is also learned that the deposits in Shanghai banks currently amount to 200 million yuan.

Foreign Nationals Considering Payment

Hua Dong News reports that income tax is scheduled to begin on the first of next month. Since the Central government sent personnel to Shanghai, they have been consulting with various parties on the collection procedures. On the foreign national side, leaders of the British, American, Italian, French, and German communities in China have agreed to consider the tax. It is believed that the friendship between China and the aforementioned countries is strong, and that this tax is common in various countries around the world, so they are unlikely to firmly refuse to pay. However, Japanese residents are still protesting.

Tobacco Industry Association Sends Letter to Ningbo Fellow-Provincials Association

Opposing Joint Government-Business Agency, Willing to Assist in Tobacco Monopoly, Joint Buying and Selling Agency Will Lead to Complete Demise

The Ministry of Finance recently announced its intention to implement a tobacco monopoly and establish a joint government-business buying and selling agency. The Shanghai Tobacco Industry Association believes that joint buying and selling would cut off the livelihood of the industry, so it has urgently requested the Ningbo Fellow-Provincials Association to assist in requesting the central government to abolish the proposal for joint buying and selling. The original text reads: "Respected Sirs, Our association has long heard that the financial authorities intend to establish a tobacco monopoly. Because it is related to the livelihood of our industry, we have previously sent a letter to your association to forward to the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry, requesting your assistance in providing relief and protection. On the 28th of last month, the Tax Bureau of the Ministry of Finance convened a discussion meeting for this matter and invited our association to send representatives to participate. According to the Tax Bureau's announcement, the tobacco monopoly has been approved by order of the Executive Yuan, and the general plan is roughly as follows: (1) A joint government-business buying and selling agency will be established with a capital of 5 million to 10 million, half government and half business, or 40% government and 60% business, half Chinese and half foreign. (2) Opinions on market organization and management will be solicited, and merchants will properly plan and implement them. (3) Administrative and business boundaries will be delineated and decided by the preparatory office. (4) The tobacco monopoly will first be piloted with Xuchang tobacco in Henan. At that time, the Tax Bureau also stated that this proposal is a general outline for the monopoly, and the detailed rules are still to be formulated. A preparatory office will be established jointly with tobacco merchants, and if tobacco merchants have any opinions, they can express them in writing in the near future. Our association has held a meeting to discuss this matter and unanimously agreed that the government is organizing a tobacco monopoly to adjust tobacco production and sales, improve tobacco quality, eliminate raw materials for private cigarettes, develop legitimate commerce, and enrich national tax revenue. Our industry should fully support and assist the government in achieving its goals. However, the establishment of a joint government-business buying and selling agency is purely for profit and exceeds the administrative scope of government control and supervision of tobacco. Regardless of the fact that our industry's capital is weak and unable to participate, even if we were able to participate, it would be impossible. Once this business agency with strong capital is established and manipulates the market and prices, each tobacco merchant with weak economic power will inevitably not survive. Even if a few can temporarily struggle to support themselves, they will have no business to operate because cigarette factories that consume tobacco will directly purchase from the company. As a result, our long-established tobacco companies will collapse and disappear due to the establishment of the joint government-business agency, and the livelihoods of hundreds of thousands of people directly and indirectly will be cut off. Although it is said that the government has no intention of competing with the people for profit, tobacco merchants are in danger of complete demise. How can this be the government's intention to protect commerce and benefit the people? Our industry believes that the government wants to achieve the goals of eliminating private cigarettes, enriching national taxes, adjusting production and sales, and improving tobacco. There are many ways to achieve these goals other than establishing a joint government-business buying and selling agency. If the government leads from above and tobacco merchants assist from below, and work together, there is no reason why it cannot be successful. Based on the above opinions, our association sent a letter to the Tax Bureau on the 3rd of this month, appealing to them to consider the livelihoods of hundreds of thousands of people directly and indirectly dependent on tobacco, and to abandon the establishment of a joint government-business buying and selling agency. Under the principle of not harming national tax revenue and not harming the interests of tobacco merchants, we will negotiate a solution and cooperate together. We have not yet received a reply to our letter. Because this matter is related to the rise and fall of our industry, and most of our industry are fellow-provincials from Ningbo, we dare to state the process and our opinions to your association. We earnestly request that you consider the livelihoods of hundreds of thousands of fellow-provincials who rely on tobacco for a living, and forward the situation to the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry, appealing to them to protect the livelihoods of tobacco merchants, abolish the joint establishment of a buying and selling agency, and devise other appropriate solutions, always with the goal of achieving both national tax revenue and the interests of tobacco merchants as the best policy. We hope that your association will handle this matter and are extremely grateful."

Domestic Leather Goods

Exports to Be Eliminated

Japanese Goods Cater to American Psychology

Our Exporters Should Improve

Leather goods have always been produced in northwestern China and have a wide export market, occupying an important position in export trade. American leather merchants have always sent specialists to Shanghai to be responsible for purchasing. Recently, Japan has realized that leather goods occupy an important position in international trade, so it has sent personnel to various parts of the northwest to purchase in large quantities, slightly select them, and ship them overseas for dumping, which has greatly affected the export market of China's leather goods industry. According to industry insiders yesterday, China's leather goods have recently been unable to gain a foothold in the American market due to Japan's large-scale shipments for dumping. In the past, American leather merchants sent specialists stationed in Shanghai by the Hudson's Bay Fur Company to be responsible for purchasing for convenience, and the annual trade reached more than one million yuan. Later, the styles of Japanese foreign leather, purple lamb, and grey squirrel goods were suitable for the American market, while the quality of Chinese exported leather was considered to be gradually changing, with sizes varying and unsuitable for use, so they switched to purchasing from Japan. However, Japanese goods are all purchased from northwestern China, only slightly selected and shipped to the United States for sale, and they have actually occupied the market, which is surprising. Therefore, if Chinese leather goods operators do not make efforts, they will inevitably be completely eliminated. Regarding grey squirrels, which China used to export the most, American merchants are now purchasing from Russia due to poor manufacturing. It is expected that leather goods exports this year will decline even further.

The Shanghai Municipal Council Rickshaw Affairs Committee recently issued a notice stating that the current licenses of rickshaw pullers of private rickshaws will expire at the end of this month. From October 1st, they should renew their licenses, which will expire at the end of September next year. From November 16th of this year, rickshaw pullers of private rickshaws who do not have new licenses and wear new armbands in a prominent place on the left arm will not be allowed to pull rickshaws. The dates for renewing licenses are stipulated as follows: (1) Licenses numbered from 1 to 5,000 should be applied for renewal from October 1st to October 20th of this year. (2) Licenses numbered from 5,001 to 8,000 should be applied for renewal from October 21st to November 4th. (3) Licenses numbered above 8,000 should be applied for renewal from November 5th to November 16th. All rickshaw pullers of private rickshaws should pay attention to carrying their current licenses and armbands to the Municipal Council Rickshaw Pullers Licensing Office on Xinzha Bote Road during the stipulated dates to apply for renewal. Please do not delay. The office hours are from 8:00 AM to 5:00 PM from Monday to Friday, 8:00 AM to 1:00 PM on Saturday, and closed on Sunday. Furthermore, the fee for renewing a new license is 50 cents in national currency within the stipulated period, and one yuan in national currency after the deadline.
