Spring and Autumn

Snippets

— (Yi Mei)

Confine a phoenix with a cage, restrain a tiger with idleness; the city imprisons crowds of people.

Looking at paintings is like buying a mountain, appreciating flowers is like taking a concubine.

The sound of the xiao is fitting under the moon, appropriate before the flowers.

The begonia severs the heart, the azalea stains the blood; who says flowers and birds are without feelings?

In the quiet of autumn nights, keeping one or two autumn insects in a vase or pot, their faint sounds are most helpful to my writing inspiration.

A person who can spend half a lifetime in leisure is a god.

Rather that my relatives and friends are all poor while I am rich alone, I would rather that my relatives and friends are all rich while I am poor alone.

Common people conduct themselves in the world by regarding trickery as the only way.

Having adorned the face while going against the heart, and blocking the eyes to prick the ears, what more can be said about such an environment?

The ugliness of people is often exposed by gold.

Wealth is the enemy of elegance, therefore elegant scholars are mostly poor. Longevity is the enemy of beauty, therefore beautiful women all have short lives.

Passing a festival while away from home, listening to the sound of rain on an autumn night, makes one want to call out, but what to do?

The monthly rose, grown in this country, can have its petals picked and boiled as a tea substitute to regulate women's menstruation.

Everyone knows that lotus petals placed in books can prevent bookworms. It is said that they can also cure rotten feet; regardless of whether they are new or old, apply several to the affected area, and they will naturally heal day by day.

Shoes... Scepter... Robe

— Qing Qu

Mr. Gu Tinglin of Kunshan's "Remaining Shoe," one shoe, has been treasured in the Gu Ancestral Hall in Qiandun Town. Even now, I still remember more than twenty years ago, when the Pingquan Studio opened a calligraphy and painting exhibition on Chengdu Road, Gu's descendants brought it to Shanghai for display, along with a handwritten copy of "The Book of Benefits and Harms to the World and the Nation." Only Gu's shoe was exceptionally large, and all who saw it were amazed, thinking that the feet of the wise men of the past had a different scale, then the greatness of his trunk and limbs could be imagined even more.

Gui Youguang was also from Kunshan. When he was young, discussing books, his grandmother loved her grandson deeply: one day, passing by his study, she said, "My son, I haven't seen your shadow for a long time, why are you silently here all day, just like a maiden?" After leaving, she closed the door with her hand, saying to herself, "My family's reading has not been effective for a long time, can the success of this child be expected?" Soon after, she brought an ivory scepter, saying, "This is what my ancestor, the Taichang Duke, held during the Xuande period to attend court; one day, you should use it." This was what Xifu himself said, but I don't know if his descendants can still preserve this ivory scepter now?

Also, Gu Dingchen, a grand secretary of the Ming Dynasty, whose great-grandson moved from Kunshan to thirty miles southeast of our county, to a place called Factory Head; his family treasured a court robe, one and a half times the length of a person, and a record-keeping scepter, about two feet tall, which they would respectfully offer every spring and autumn for sacrifices: now I don't know where it has ended up. Reciting the poem by Mr. Yang Zixiang of Doushan, "The grand secretary's career has melted like ice, the robe and scepter drift away, lamenting the past dynasty; before the ancestral hall of the prime minister, turning my head again, my heart is ashamed, and wine is hard to wash away," it makes one unable to stop sighing.

Ginkgo

— Damu

Ginkgo, commonly known as white fruit, has very tall trees, with dense branches and leaves like an umbrella. It is best to enjoy the cool under a ginkgo tree in the summer, and the biggest advantage is that it doesn't have spiny caterpillars and wild silkworms falling on people like other trees. The fruit is about the same as an apricot, with yellow skin. Removing the outer flesh, the white shell inside is the white fruit. Normally, white fruits are knocked down from the tree, and the outer flesh is left to rot, because it is easier.

It is not easy to find ginkgo trees in Shanghai; Bansong Garden, Zhaofeng Park...don't have any, right? Ginkgo trees are indeed difficult to grow. Often, those planted by grandfathers may not have white fruits to eat by the time the grandsons are around. However, Shanghainese do not have to worry about not having white fruits to eat. When the autumn wind first rises, the sound of people selling white fruits on the streets appears. The sentences are really like lyrics, listen: "Hot white fruits, fragrant, glutinous and soft, white fruits bigger than goose eggs, one copper coin for three, two copper coins for seven, come and count if you want to eat, pick and pass if you don't!"

According to a friend, these words for selling white fruits can be sung as a qingyi flowing plate, the words of course need to be added or subtracted a bit. Upon further reflection, there is a small discovery. For example, where are there white fruits as big as goose eggs! The peddlers insist on shouting "goose egg big," which is clearly a deception. In fact, in this big Shanghai market, unrealistic publicity fills the ears, and the peddlers' few words of description are already considered honest. Moreover, two copper coins can get you one cheaper, which is an even more "realistic" preferential treatment.

There are two ginkgo trees at the back door of my uncle's house in my hometown. When I was sixteen in my hometown, they were five or six arm spans around. In the past eight or nine years, I imagine they have grown even thicker. However, I recently heard that they were forcibly bought at the lowest price by the old local gentry in the village, on the grounds that they hindered the feng shui of his new building and were sawed down. The gentry's mind is so ridiculously pedantic, and my impoverished uncle was deprived of the only remaining "ancestral blessing" for no reason, which is too pitiful.

From my uncle's ginkgo trees, I also thought of a tragic "social news" from a few days ago. A peddler who borrowed "usurious money" to sell white fruits was killed when the local hoodlums from Jiangyin Street demanded money and didn't get it, kicking his own child to death... The path of life is full of thorns. Writing about ginkgo here, I suddenly feel gloomy...

— Mingxin

The recent rise of Hebei Ping Opera in Shanghai's theater scene can be said to be unexpected. It should aim to win the sympathy of the general audience from an artistic perspective without being offensive. Only then can it be considered top-notch. The wording was elegant and poetic, and their ability to avoid vulgarity in their charm was truly commendable. The reputation they have earned is indeed not accidental. Outside, it is drizzling, and a gust of wind blows the rain threads dancing wildly in the air, making the entire sky grayish-white. The little bird in the cage is just chirping, perhaps feeling that autumn is too bleak and frightening. Keep falling and blowing away all the heat and annoyance.

Looking back at my colleagues, each of them is buried in their writing, forgetting spring, forgetting summer, and forgetting autumn. For the sake of life, they have abandoned nature. No, please put down your pens and look outside, autumn will give you a profound feeling!

Small Local Chronicles

Casual Talk about Beihai

— Nailing

The Beihai that this article is about is not the Beihai in Beiping, but a small trading port in the Southern Circuit of Guangdong Province. I'm afraid that readers have never heard of this small trading port before? However, since the Beihai Japanese Residents Incident occurred, it has been featured in the newspapers every day, and the name Beihai has become less unfamiliar.

What kind of place is Beihai actually? Well, let me tell you: Beihai is a small trading port with only a few straight and a few horizontal roads. Although this small trading port is a rather important port in the Southern Circuit of Guangdong, with large cargo ships sailing to Hong Kong, Guangzhou Bay, and Haiphong almost every other day, a pier where ships can dock has not yet been built to this day. Ships arriving from Hong Kong anchor far out at sea, and passengers and cargo are transported to land by small sampans.

When Beihai was first opened as a trading port, elders said that it was a very promising port. In addition to the specialties of Hepu and other places near Beihai and the nearby villages, such as seafood, bird's nests, sandworms, piglets, grass bags, etc., which were exported through the port of Beihai, the specialties of Guangxi Province and the specialties of Qinzhou and Leizhou were also concentrated in Beihai and then transported out. At the same time, flour, groceries, etc. imported from Hong Kong were mostly transshipped from Beihai to Hepu, Qinlei, and even Guangxi Province. Even the trade between Beihai and Haiphong in Annam used to occupy a very important position, but since Wuzhou in Guangxi was opened as a trading port, most of the goods imported and exported from Guangxi no longer needed to be transshipped through Beihai. On the other hand, the production volume of various specialties has decreased, and the market in Hong Kong has been hit by goods from other places. For example, in the past, cargo ships sailing from Beihai to Hong Kong were always loaded with piglets, but since Dalian pork was dumped in Hong Kong, the piglet business in Beihai has been affected. As a result, the commerce of Beihai has declined sharply, and it has also affected the construction of municipal administration. If we searched all over Beihai, there would probably only be thirty or forty old-fashioned crank telephones, and there wouldn't be many cars either. Not to mention the roads, there is probably only Zhuhai Middle Road in Beihai that is sixteen feet wide.

Beihai is located in the southwest of Hepu County. Hepu County is a famous pearl-producing area. The Hepu of "The Pearl Returns to Hepu" is here. Hepu still retains a "Dongpo Pavilion", which is said that Su Dongpo once lived in Beihai and Hepu for some time.

The languages of Beihai and Hepu are mostly Cantonese, with the exception of some Hakka dialects; however, it differs somewhat from Cantonese in Guangzhou. Speaking of cultural life, it is a bit too "that." After searching all over Hepu and Beihai, only one Hepu County Middle School was found. This middle school is located in the northeastern suburbs of Beihai City. The architecture is not bad, and the affiliated library can also be accessed by outsiders for reading; but when the author returned to his hometown to visit his family three years ago, there was not even a newspaper office in the Beihai area.

The lives of farmers in the Beihai area are very difficult, so most of the sons and daughters of farmers in Qinlian run out to become soldiers. Chen Mingshu and Xiang Hanping, famous generals in Guangdong, are from Hepu County, and Chen Jitang, who recently stepped down, is from Qin County. As for the lower-level officers and soldiers of the 19th Route Army, almost more than half of them are from Qinlian. In the past, the recruitment of troops in various units in Guangdong all went to Qinlian, which had a large number of surplus farmers. Another reason is that the people of Qinlian are able to endure hardship and are able to obey. Recruiting people from Qinlian to be soldiers is most suitable.

However, the people who come to Qinlian to recruit soldiers often also use deceptive means. For example, the recruitment office sends local ruffians and hooligans deep into the villages to win over the general young farmers. These farmers are falling into a state of idleness because of the economic downturn in the countryside. The ruffians and hooligans pretend to be fond of them and encourage them to gamble and prostitute themselves. At the same time, they also lend them money to use. After a considerable period of time, they use force to force them to repay the debt. They often have no way to repay the debt, so they use the means of enticement and coercion to force them to agree to become enlisted soldiers.

These enlisted soldiers are transported from various villages to Beihai, and then transported from Beihai to Guangzhou for training, but some of them regret it halfway. They do not want to leave their hometown, so they have to take the opportunity to escape. The author once personally witnessed a person who was unwilling to board the ship to Guangzhou in Beihai. He hid in the hold of a sailboat, and later jumped into the sea after being searched. As a result, he was shot in the head by the officers on the ship with a pistol, and the blood that flowed out dyed almost the entire sea red.

Shenbao Medical Supplement

The Authority of the Chef (Part 2)

— Huang Yiqing

You must know that fire is the only tool that the chef uses to earn a living. Anything that is eaten must be cooked to perfection with proper heat; utensils used for serving food must be exposed to sufficient heat to ensure hygiene; and cloths used for wiping utensils must be thoroughly sterilized with heat. From the perspective of disease-causing organisms, your greatest authority is that you are the executioner who directly uses fire to kill them. If you are careless and negligent, they will be happy to take advantage of it, and you will become a traitor who condones disease-causing organisms in harming people. Of course, on the one hand, overcooking food can reduce the digestibility of proteins. For example, overcooked eggs are naturally less digestible than lightly cooked ones. However, as a chef, you should be skilled at cooking food, knowing how to cook it just right, how to cook it until well done, and how to cook it to perfection. You should be able to master these skills through practice.

You must also know that "cleanliness" is the only "selling point" of a chef. If your person, hands, and fingernails are not clean, your appearance will not be good. If the knives, spatulas, ladles, pots, and other utensils are not cleaned properly, your appearance will not be good. If the rice, fish, meat, vegetables, and other raw foods are not washed clean, your appearance will not be good. If raw foods are not purchased fresh and clean, the appearance of the food will not be good, which means your own appearance is not good. If cooked foods are not properly protected and are exposed to flies, dust, and dirt before being eaten, it is all because of your poor appearance. As Wu Lefu said, not having "face" is for this reason. From the perspective of disease-causing organisms, your greatest duty is that you are the watchman who is responsible for preventing them from breaking in. If you are muddled and negligent, and your defenses are lax, then don't blame them for tearing down your stage! Cleanliness is not the same as hygiene, and there are indeed many aspects to hygiene. However, from a chef's perspective, it can be said that cleanliness is always hygienic or close to hygienic.

However, further, when a chef seasons food, the flavor and intensity must be tailored to the taste of the host or customer. The allocation, preparation, and protection of food cannot be entirely under the chef's control. For example, if the host only likes to eat meat and does not like green vegetables, or if the customer prefers fried dishes and does not eat stir-fried or stewed dishes, then in addition to fulfilling their duties to the best of their ability, chefs must also rely on the host and customer to "help themselves" and make wise choices. In families, the housewife who manages the household affairs must have this kind of common sense and ability to direct. How many large families hire chefs to cook their food? In most families, the housewife must personally handle everything in the kitchen, large and small. In a small number of families, even if they hire servants, the housewife must be careful every step of the way and train them thoroughly before they can be "in tune." Then I must always ask: In recent years, has the general education of women in our country provided in-depth training in such practical knowledge and skills? I'm afraid that even now, this is still something that those who advocate reforming education should think about supplementing.

Finally, there is one more point that is worth noting. If a chef has tuberculosis, venereal disease, or leprosy, it is easy to know that they should not be hired. However, if they appear to be healthy on the outside and are "clean," but are secretly a permanent, temporary, or intermittent carrier of fecal-oral or droplet-transmitted diseases, how dangerous is that? According to the author's speculation, in the future, when hygiene has reached its peak, not only will the chefs in restaurants everywhere be subject to public health examinations at all times, but also the chefs hired by families will have to add a clause to their contracts stating that a certain "great doctor" has signed a certificate proving that the person is not a carrier of any disease before people dare to hire them. Employment agencies may have to imitate the meat inspection in slaughterhouses in Europe and the United States, and hire experts to reside in the agency to inspect for bacteria and viruses and sign certificates of health before people dare to use them! When hiring chefs or servants now, you should at least ask if they have had cholera, typhoid fever, dysentery, diphtheria, pneumonia, meningococcal meningitis, etc. recently, and you should choose those who have not had these diseases to hire, to avoid mistakenly hiring automatic carriers after illness (I can't think of a good way to deal with those passive carriers).

The Nanjing Health Education Committee held a training class for school chefs last year. It is hoped that this kind of committee can expand its authority to manage the health education of the public and hold more general training classes for chefs, cooks, or housewives. It is also hoped that various places will follow suit.

Also, the Nanjing Municipal Health Office seems to have established some kind of model kitchen. If it is indeed considered simple and practical and can be promoted nationwide, it is hoped that the contents of this model kitchen can be announced so that everyone can follow suit or observe some of the concepts that a kitchen should have.

Investigation Report on the Sanitary Conditions of Xiaoshi, Zhejiang (Part 1)

— Shen Songnian

Although Xiaoshi is a small town, it is located on the main road of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway, and water and land transportation is developed early, and the townspeople are accustomed to fashion, and their lives combine luxury and simplicity, but the people's wisdom is very low, and various sanitary facilities cannot be realized as scheduled, which is very regrettable. As a result of the continuous efforts of the authorities over the years, a rough scale has been achieved, and it can be said to be unique compared to the remote rural areas, but it is still far behind the big cities! ——This is of course a very big morbid state, and there are reasons for it, and it cannot be entirely blamed on the ineffectiveness of the sanitary authorities. It is simply a case of "a clever woman cannot cook without rice," but the educational community and our medical community should also bear a considerable responsibility, which is undeniable. Now, based on my limited knowledge of the general sanitary conditions of Xiaoshi, I summarize a few points below, which can be regarded as a reference for the sanitary authorities to improve:

(A) Regarding Medical Administration

(1) Siltation of City Rivers

The Xiaoshi market is not yet prosperous enough to have a tap water plant, and the drinking water needed by the residents in the city center is entirely supplied by the city river. Although public wells have been established, they are only a drop in the bucket. Once the river water is shallow and dry in the hot summer, it even ferments and emits a foul odor. Pedestrians cover their noses. It is the main base of all kinds of germs, which hinders hygiene more than anything else. Therefore, it is advisable to find a way to dredge it, because it is not only related to the drinking water of the people, but also hinders fire prevention. It is recently heard that Mr. Wu Xinmu, a local gentry and captain of the fire brigade, and others specially convened a meeting to discuss the dredging plan. If it can be realized as scheduled, it will be a great act of benevolence, benefiting the masses of the people.

(2) Uncleanliness of Waterways

The Tanghe outside Tangqiao is the source of the city river. Therefore, the failure to improve the Tanghe affects the water quality of the city river and the health of the people. If flowers are often found and the odor fills the sky, it is the main cause of the prevalence of epidemics. It is hoped that the authorities will order the health police to conduct strict and thorough investigations at any time. If any are found, they should be strictly eliminated on the spot and the households should be strictly investigated and severely punished to punish them as an example and to maintain hygiene and respect for the lives of the people.

(3) Lack of Public Toilets

Often, in many places, residents do not know hygiene, their knowledge is low, and they set up unhygienic toilets at will, even open-air cesspools, which are very harmful to the health of the people. The gas in the toilets is enough to sicken healthy people, and the only media for epidemics—flies and mosquitoes—like to gather in this filth, and then bring the germs to food and drink, misleading mankind. Therefore, the sanitary authorities have repeatedly ordered strict elimination. However, in fact, simply implementing passive measures without actively spreading public toilets has many drawbacks. For example, although unhygienic toilets have been eliminated, ignorant people still turn a blind eye and instead intensify their efforts to scatter them everywhere, resulting in piles of feces and urine, such as in bridge holes and alleys.

(4) Failure to Remove Stinking Ponds

Anyone who has been to Xiaoshi knows that the Shashibang (commonly known as the Garbage Pond, the name of the pond is Garbage, and the degree of its filth can be known) here is a famous stinking pond, and it is the best factory for manufacturing epidemics. Residents have no public morals, do not pay attention to public health, and some families even simply pour garbage into the pond and wash their chamber pots. As a result, the pond water becomes more and more silted up, the water quality becomes more and more turbid, and in the hot summer, mosquitoes and flies gather, the pond water ferments and sublimes, and the stench fills the sky, which is enough to help the prevalence of epidemics. It is hoped that the sanitary authorities will take measures to remove it as soon as possible. The passive measure is to order residents not to pour garbage into the pond at will, and to sprinkle disinfectant water at any time. The active measure is that, in any case, the pond water cannot be used by the people. In the current economic downturn where it is difficult to raise funds, it is impossible to improve it. It is better to simply fill it in and then mark it for sale. The proceeds will be used for local public health construction to benefit the people.

(5) Resident Population

The entire county has about 350,000 people, and this town accounts for more than one-seventh of the county's population. (To be continued)

The Importance of Public Health Nurses

— Ji Jingshou

The development of medical and health construction in China in recent years has been rapid, and there is indeed a trend of rapid progress. The development of health construction undertakings can reduce disease rates and mortality rates, and can promote people's health, prolong people's lives, increase work ability, entertain the body and mind, and increase the country's international status, which is also an undeniable fact. The personnel who can be responsible for promoting and developing this medical and health construction undertaking are public health doctors, nurses, midwives, health inspectors, and other medical personnel; among them, public health nurses are the main tool and driving force for promoting this work, and they are also the only public health nurses who can go deep into the grassroots to do the most basic work. Whether in prosperous cities, remote poor villages, schools, families, institutions, and factories, there are footprints of public health nurses; especially in poor and remote areas where doctors cannot be hired, public health nurses can bury themselves in hard work and effort at a very low salary.

(1) Publicize and instill medical and health knowledge, the principles of diseases, methods of maintaining health, and how to prevent infectious diseases to the public.

(2) Enable the sick to receive appropriate treatment and care, in order to achieve recovery and restore physical and mental health.

(3) Actively contact and cooperate with local medical and health institutions and other social service organizations.

(4) Assist the people in solving various problems that are harmful to health.

Whether the health undertaking in a place is developed or not can be said to depend entirely on whether the public health nurse is talented, whether they work hard, whether they can teach the people, and whether they are willing to cooperate with others. Therefore, the work of public health nurses is closely related to the development of health undertakings, the health of the people, the strength of the country, and the rise and fall of the nation.

Since the work of public health nurses is as important as described above and their mission is extremely bright, public health nurses have indeed occupied a basic position in modern medical and health construction undertakings. Indeed, public health nurses are the fresh troops and vanguards responsible for vigorously promoting modern medical and health construction undertakings.

Common Knowledge of Diseases Q&A

— Cheng Hanzhang

(92) Gout (Part 1)

(Q) What is gout?

(A) Gout is a disease caused by the accumulation of uric acid in the body that cannot be excreted from the kidneys. Clinically, it causes an inflammatory state in various joints.

(Q) What is the English name for gout?

(A) It is called Gout in English, Gicht in German, and Arthritis Urica in Latin.

(Q) What are the causes of gout?

(A) The causes of gout are related to constitution and heredity. People with a family history of uric acid are often more likely to suffer from gout. In terms of one's own body, people who eat too much meat and drink excessively are also prone to this disease. Therefore, wealthy people are more likely to get it than poor people.

(Q) Is gout related to age and gender?

(A) Men are more likely to get it than women; the age of onset is from 30 to 50 years old.

(Q) What are the symptoms of gout?

(A) Gout is a disease that occurs in attacks, and there is a distinction between acute attack symptoms and chronic symptoms.

(Q) What are the symptoms of an acute attack?

(A) It occurs suddenly, but there are generally prodromal symptoms such as indigestion, general fatigue, and mental depression. Other symptoms include traction pain and calf muscle spasms, and there may also be fever.

(Q) What symptoms appear at the time of the attack?

(A) It mostly starts at night or in the morning and evening. First, a very severe pain occurs in the toe joint of one big toe, which is called podagra. This pain is very intense and cannot tolerate slight pressure. The affected joint is red, swollen, and hot. This gout attack lasts from night to morning and gradually subsides. However, the joint swelling does not completely disappear and recurs again the next night. This lasts for half a week.

(Q) Is gout over after it occurs once?

(A) No, it generally recurs once or several times after a few weeks or days.

(Q) Does gout attack other parts besides the toes?

(A) Later, it gradually invades the joints other than the big toe, such as the tarsal joint, ankle joint, and knee joint. It also invades the upper limb joints, hand joints, and little finger joints. All distal joints of the limb bones are easily invaded.

(Q) Besides the small joints, can gout invade the large joints?

(A) Large joints can also be invaded, and there is a possibility of attacks in the hip joint and shoulder joint.

(Q) After repeated attacks of gout, what abnormalities will occur in the joints?

(A) There are cases of joint deformity, and it can also become chronic gout. (To be continued)

Domestic Medicinal Plants (Continued)

— Zhou Mengbai

6. Peppermint Mentha arvensis, L.var.piperascens, Holmes.

(Plant) Grows naturally in fields and damp places by the roadside, can be cultivated, is a perennial herb. The entire plant is densely covered with short hairs. Leaves are opposite, with short petioles, oblong, with serrated edges and pointed tips. Short-stalked verticillaster inflorescences grow from the leaf axils, blooming with small, pale purple labiate flowers in summer and autumn. The achenes are small and ovoid.

(Cultivation) In late November, the land is prepared, and the underground stems are planted in dry fields with rows 2.5 feet wide. For paddy fields, each row should be 8 feet wide, slightly raised, and planted in two lines. Fertilizers such as soybean meal, human manure and urine, and artificial fertilizers are used. Harvesting takes place three times in China: late June, mid-August, and mid-October. Each acre yields about 250 catties of dried herbs. Peppermint oil can be extracted from the dried herbs by steam distillation. The yield is 0.8-1.8% of the dried herbs. The oil content is highest in the second harvest and lowest in the first.

(Crude Drug) Peppermint Leaf Folium Menthae is collected and dried. The product is oval or lanceolate, about 3-7 cm long, with irregular serrations, and a pointed tip. The leaf surface is sparsely covered with villous hairs. It has a unique aromatic odor and a cooling property.

(Components) The entire herb contains about 1% essential oil. The total Menthol CilH2oO content in the essential oil is 70-90% (free Menthol 65-85% Ester 3-8%), and the rest are Menthon CioHi8O Menthenon-3 CilHi60 I-Limonen 3.4 Hexenolphenylacetat C2H5-CH=CHCH2-CH2-O-CO-CH2-C6H5 Aethyln-amylkston C2H5COC5H11 etc.

(Medicinal Uses) The entire herb is steam distilled to produce peppermint oil, which can then be used to produce Mentholum (Bureau of Formulas). Menthol can be used to correct taste and odor. Menthol and peppermint oil are also consumed in large quantities in the manufacture of toothpaste and confectionery.

Japanese peppermint oil is favored for its high Monthol content, but it has a slight bitter taste and is not as fragrant as that produced in Europe and America. Therefore, Japanese peppermint oil is mainly used as a raw material for Menthol production, while European and American peppermint oil is used in confectionery. Mitcham oil produced in Mitcham, England, is considered the best, with excellent aroma and is highly valued.

Hospitalization and Convalescence Costs Three Cents Per Day

— Ding Huikang

The Success of the Golden State's Medical Control – How is the Health of the Nation's People Guaranteed?

For only three cents a day, you can get three weeks or more of free hospitalization and convalescence. Are you willing to pay this small amount to avoid a huge expense that is outside of your annual household budget? Currently, 500,000 people in the United States have joined health insurance. This health insurance business is becoming increasingly popular, with tens of thousands of new members joining each month.

For example, Mr. So-and-so, the 100,000th member of the Associated Hospital Service of N.Y., is a completely healthy person. However, if this person suddenly becomes ill and needs hospitalization (approximately one in ten people require hospitalization), with the small membership fee paid on a regular basis, he can choose to stay in a semi-private room in one of the 137 city hospitals for 21 days free of charge. If continued hospitalization is required, he will still enjoy a 25% discount.

New York City's insurance fee serves as a model for the 24 large-scale "hospital insurance companies" (or health insurance companies). The minimum premium in Cleveland and Birmingham is 60 cents per month, 65 cents in Rochester, and 75 cents in Sacramento and New Orleans.

Hospitals charge the following fees for patients sent by such insurance companies:

Fee for one day's stay: $15

Fee for two days' stay: $20

Fee for three days' stay: $23

From the fourth day onwards, the daily fee is $6.50.

Hospitals welcome these patients, as it reduces the number of free patients. Although doctors do not receive any special benefits from this type of hospital income, they still welcome these insured patients, because patients do not have to bear hospital expenses and can more easily afford doctors' fees.

Dr. Kimball of Baylor University in Texas City was the first founder of health insurance. In 1919, he insured 1,250 school teachers for a premium of 50 cents per person per month. Due to its success, the health insurance business attracted the attention of the general public.

Six years later, in 1935, Miss Fenling Huxite in New York City joined forces with several apartment staff to start this business. Within a year, the total number of members reached 84,000. Today, it has exceeded 107,000, with 5,000 new members joining each month. The most amazing thing is that this matter has never been promoted through advertising, and yet the insurance business has spread without wings.

Dr. Kimball's original facilities are no longer sufficient for the current 18,000 members. Therefore, he is currently planning to build two new hospitals in Texas City, and several other locations are also in preparation. (To be continued)

Supplement of Shenbao, Local Edition

Talks

How Was the Fengtai Incident Resolved?

— Fang

The newspaper reported on the 19th that a sudden conflict had occurred between the Chinese and Japanese armies in Fengtai. Feng Zhian's troops were surrounded, a certain company commander was captured, and gunshots erupted. The two sides were in a stalemate. When I saw this news, I was quite shocked, thinking that such a serious matter would be even more serious than the Chengdu and Beihai incidents, or even expand, creating a third new record following the "September 18th" and "January 28th" incidents. This was not out of the question.

Therefore, I was eagerly looking forward to the newspapers on the 20th, wondering how the situation would develop after one night. To my surprise, when I opened the newspapers on the morning of the 20th, they boldly declared that the Fengtai incident had been resolved smoothly, misunderstandings had been cleared, and the company commander had been released. Such a serious problem had been resolved and reconciled in less than 24 hours. Wasn't this an unexpected piece of good news in our eyes?

Naturally, we never hope that the situation of such unfortunate incidents will escalate or be prolonged. If misunderstandings are cleared and the company commander is released, even if we cannot say that we have won a diplomatic victory, we have at least regained some face. However, I do not know the reason for the rapid resolution of this unfortunate incident. Was it due to the intervention of the Hebei authorities? Or was it because the Japanese side made an extraordinary retreat, seeking to appease the situation and muddle through? It is really difficult to understand how such a bad debt was settled in the end.

According to a Tianjin dispatch from a certain newspaper, since the Japanese North China Garrison Army was strengthened, disputes have repeatedly arisen in the Fengtai area. The soldiers stationed there often feel oppressed. Unexpectedly, at 5:00 p.m. on the 18th, a unit of the Japanese army was conducting exercises in Fengtai and intended to pass through our garrison camp. Our army tried to stop them, but the Japanese army refused to listen, and a conflict broke out. Whether the cause of this incident was as reported by a certain newspaper is still unknown, but it is unlikely to be completely false. Fengtai is an important territory of our country in North China. In our own territory, our own troops are stationed, yet such serious consequences have occurred. What kind of world is this? If we look at it this way, I cannot help but doubt how the Fengtai incident was resolved, and especially how it was resolved smoothly. Assuming that this matter can be resolved peacefully based on the two principles of not losing sovereignty and not losing territory, it would be a great blessing. However, if everything is disregarded, and we completely submit and completely comply with the will of the other party to achieve a peaceful resolution, such a resolution is worse than no resolution at all. I very much hope for peace and love peace, but peace has its limits and its way of speaking. Therefore, Confucius said, "To know harmony and to harmonize, but not to regulate it by propriety, is also not permissible." I would change his saying to, "To know harmony and to harmonize, but to forget the interests of the nation, is absolutely not permissible."

As I was finishing this article, I saw yesterday's newspaper, which said that all of our troops stationed in Fengtai had been withdrawn and moved to Zhao Jia Zhuang south of Fengtai. If this is the case, then in the area where Chinese and Japanese troops clashed, our army retreats one place; if there are clashes in ten places, then our army retreats ten places. I don't know how many Fengtai's our country can withdraw from? How many Zhao Jia Zhuang's can we station in? This is also considered a peaceful resolution, truly, I am speechless.

A Visit to the Mu Du Preservation of Chastity Bureau (Part 1)

— Fang Zhou

(Special Report from This Newspaper) In ancient times, chaste women were praised by sages and commended by emperors. Therefore, we can still see many chastity archways and shrines of female martyrs existing in various places; moreover, those chastity archways and shrines are all inlaid with an imperial decree or a constitutional decree. At that time, this glory and greatness can be imagined. But under the residual poison of this glory and greatness, up to now, I don't know how many innocent women have been crushed to death, and I don't know how many women have lightly ruined their lifelong happiness!

Chastity is regarded as private property by most men, and only women have the obligation to maintain chastity. In our country, in the past and even now, not only do men have the right to force women to maintain chastity, but also women themselves are willing to live this desolate life of a widow before death.

Institutions that encourage chastity, such as the Qingjie Hall, Anjie Bureau, and Baojie Bureau, have emerged in the environment of these sages, virtuous people, and philanthropists praising chastity; in the inland of our country, where the cannibalistic old etiquette forces are still very strong, such abnormal phenomena are still very common. Moreover, those gentlemen and masters, even if they marry four or five concubines themselves, righteously do not allow their wives and daughters to ruin their reputation (?). Therefore, they feel that the praise of chastity cannot be abolished under any circumstances.

I have visited the Anjie Bureau in Suzhou before, but it has now been merged into the Women and Children Relief Institute; today, the only remaining one is the Baojie Bureau in Mu Du.

Baojie Bureau, as the name suggests, we can know that it is an institution to protect chastity. Yesterday, for the convenience of going to Suzhou, I made a special trip to visit the bureau.

The bureau was founded in the years of the former Qing Guangxu (between 1886-1890), and to this day, it has been around for forty years. The founder was Feng Peizhi, a native of the county. — It is said that Feng Peizhi was the treasurer of the Jiangsu Daotai Yamen, and his wife's younger brother was the one who worked in the treasury. Once, his wife's younger brother embezzled tens of thousands of taels of treasury silver. After Feng discovered this, he was afraid of implicating the national law, so he diverted the money to create this Baojie Bureau; thus, the shortage was used to report to his superiors. Therefore, the Baojie Bureau is still a thing of property defense.

I entered the walled gate, and saw a plaque with the words "Baojie Bureau" hanging in the middle. After passing through a large courtyard, there was a very large hall. There were two osmanthus trees on both sides of the courtyard, and the fragrance of osmanthus flowers kept drilling into my nostrils; in the center of the hall was a statue of Guan Gong, next to which was a wooden couplet written by Feng himself. I only remember the second line, "Embezzling public funds, men steal and women prostitute." This may be to express himself, or perhaps to warn others.

After passing through another courtyard, there was another small hall. The office and reception room were also here. On the wall hung a sign with the names of chaste women and the number of people in their families, using sentences praising chastity, such as "Cao Bozhou," to number each chaste woman.

I had broken into three or four courtyards in a row, and had not encountered a single person. This made me a little suspicious, wondering if I had run into a cold temple or ancestral hall. But I finally plucked up my courage, like an explorer, and continued to break into the inside, turning corners and asking at the half-closed doors, only hoping to meet someone to talk to.

It was not until I pushed open the last door that I heard voices inside. I followed the voices and saw several old women working there.

Here, there are sixty to seventy square flat houses, each with a narrow, low veranda in front. Each house is inhabited by a chaste woman and her children. In addition to a bed, there are also many utensils piled up in the house, and each veranda has a clay stove, where the chaste women cook their own dishes and food. Further in is a Buddhist hall, but this Buddhist hall is just like the situation outside, appearing very messy and dilapidated. At this time, there were seven or eight chaste women embroidering in the Buddhist hall. They were very surprised to see me, an uninvited guest, but none of them came to inquire. After looking at me, they still buried their heads in their needlework.

Road

— Li Yinfei

My friend and I came out of the hotel after 2:00 a.m. It was early autumn, and the wind felt very refreshing. The road was quiet, and streetcars jingled past. A policeman was leaning against a telephone pole, listless. Rickshaw pullers were running quietly, as if afraid of waking people up. Wanting to enjoy the night scenery of the autumn streets, a rickshaw puller came up, but I shook my head to indicate that I didn't want to go home yet, even though my feet were walking in that direction.

A rickshaw brushed past me. I didn't pay attention, because experience told me that it was probably a dancing girl going home with sore legs. But suddenly a clear voice floated into my ears: "Hello!"

"Hello," like an echo in an empty valley, I replied habitually. But when I looked up, I only saw a back view, and in the dim light, I couldn't recognize whose back it was.

My mind was racing, almost without thinking, I waved to a rickshaw in the distance and called it over.

The rickshaw puller smiled cunningly at me. I ignored him and just pointed forward with my hand: "Catch up! Hurry!"

Gradually, we were getting closer, but I still couldn't remember whose back it was. But looking at their so-called "airplane hairstyle" and the fact that there were two people in the rickshaw, and it was the time when the dance halls were closing, I could only awkwardly shout again: "Hello!"

With the shout, one person turned around, while the other lowered their head even further. The person who turned around had a strange face.

I ordered the rickshaw to go faster and pass them. I looked back and saw that the person who had lowered their head had thick, dark eyelashes and large eyes. — A familiar face that I couldn't remember where I had seen before.

But finally I remembered: "Oh, it's you, Suyue!"

"Going home? Why are you walking back alone so late?"

"How about we go eat something together? I have a lot to talk to you about."

"It's too late," she paused, "Alright."

So we went to a Cantonese restaurant.

As soon as we sat down, the dancing girl surnamed Zhou stood up alertly again: "Mary, my head hurts a lot, I'm going back first."

I knew what she meant, so I smiled at her and said, "Miss Zhou, please don't misunderstand, we are just classmates from the past."

"Aren't we now?" The woman surnamed Zhou smiled. I knew there was a deep meaning in that smile.

"Of course not. Now I'm a dancing girl, and he's a young master. We are walking on extreme paths!"

"Suyue, don't deliberately distort the meaning in the words, okay?"

"I'm called Mary now!"

"Isn't Mary still Suyue?"

She seemed not to have heard my words and suddenly asked: "How is life lately? Are you married?"

"Yes, I'm married. How about you?"

"I've also been married and have a child, but I'm divorced, but the child is still alive and by my side." She said it very stubbornly.

"Which dance hall are you working at now?"

"I don't want you to come and watch me dance. Besides, I'm going to Hong Kong in a few days. Business in Shanghai is very bad, and there are too many acquaintances."

"Don't you want to see me? For the sake of our past friendship, I think I can help you a little."

"Thank you, I'm fine now."

Next, we talked about the past. I wanted to use the past to make her believe that I really wanted to help her, but none of it worked. She seemed not to understand and only said some irrelevant things.

The next day, I ran all over the dance halls in Shanghai, but I couldn't find her. I only met the woman surnamed Zhou, and the woman surnamed Feng also refused to leave her residence. A few days later, I went there again, and Miss Zhou gave me a note and said: "Mary left for Hong Kong yesterday. This note was written earlier because she told me to give it to you after she left Shanghai, so I kept it until now."

I tore it up without looking at it, because I knew what she was going to say.

Are we walking on extreme paths?

Cao Xiaoying's Yu Qing Ting

Zhongxi (1040) 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening "Beauty and the Wind"

The spring breeze in February brings new omens. Heavenly winds blow down the sounds of Buxu. Looking up and gazing at the sky, there is a cloud ladder that can be climbed. I see him, with a journey of ten thousand miles ahead of him. Rising straight up and riding the green clouds. All because the east wind intentionally lifts him up. Showing his glory to the fullest and standing out from the crowd. A fairy skirt is left for swallows. Several elegant melodies harmonize with orioles. I really don't know, where is the flute and jade sheng being played. This tune is not originally from heaven. It is said that the beauty is good at singing and dancing and skillfully playing the zheng. Let's see, gracefully like the shadow of a startled goose. As light as a flying swallow in the sky. Like Cai Wenji's Eighteen Songs of the Hu Jia. Like Xiang Ling playing the zither, sounding with a clanging sound. Like a song of Zhaojun's Lament on the pipa. Like a clever red pocket and light thief. I look at him, the plain silk is tailored into thin sleeves. The Lingbo gauze robe is clean and without dust. A pair of jade arms dance with the wind. Gladly learning Ku Deng's graceful posture. All because of the shameless, frivolous appearance of the rascal. Green Pearl guards against someone falling from the building. I'm just afraid that the willow branches are soft, delicate, and powerless. Therefore, a red silk thread is tied to the feet on the first floor. Sometimes, the wind is upside down, flipping the shadow. Playfully imitating Yang Guifei emerging from the bath, not the true face of Mount Lu. Where can a soulmate be found in this world? If it is that one day she falls into the world of dust. It provokes the cold eyes of many bystanders. Therefore, standing firmly and not losing your footing. Stop where you should and stay put. Don't break the paper tiger. Still guarding against sudden storms and heavy winds morning and evening. But originally, human life is like a dream. Even drifting with the wind is like floating clouds. Nothing more than the same ups and downs.

Xing Ruiting's Three Smiles

Linji (1220) 9:05 PM to 10:00 PM

Opening "The Western Chamber Borrowing a Room"

Going to the capital to take the exam and arriving in Puzhou. Crows in several arrays of the setting sun are red. Hastily wanting to find a place to stay. Zhang Xiangong, to dispel his worries, walks into the Puji Temple. He bows to the monk, Xiao Facong. He sincerely bows in the Buddhist hall. He burns incense silently, praying for good luck to come. May the crimson-clad judge secretly mark him as the top scholar in the capital exams. At that time, the Great Hero's Palace will be magnificent. The solemn Buddhist statues are all majestic. After bowing, he wanders through the Buddhist hall. Surely, the flowers and trees lead to a secluded path through the Zen room. Suddenly, the tinkling of pendants and earrings comes from the inner courtyard. A pretty girl, lightly paints her eyebrows with the colors of spring. Tingting, like a fairy. With narrow golden lotuses, she moves through the air. Her beautiful appearance is like Xu Feiqiong. I hear that she is the daughter of the Prime Minister of Pu Dong. Their hearts are connected. The autumn waves turned when she left. His soul had already gone to the sky. Zhang Xiangong has a plan in mind. He borrows a secluded room to study in. Fortunately, Fang Ding is understanding. Naturally matching the beautiful couple. A lifetime of happiness is endless.

Movies

The Revitalized Jin Cheng

The First Film to be Shown: "Women's Rights"

The Jin Cheng Grand Theater on Beijing Road has been under repair for a month. Now it is completely completed, and the interior and exterior of the theater have been completely renovated. The first film to be released has been selected, starring Hu Die, entitled "Women's Rights." Below is a brief description of the theater's situation:

The interior and exterior walls of the theater have been repainted, adorned and embellished, resplendent and magnificent, like entering a palace. The wall lamps and chandeliers have also been replaced with new-style electric torches, which are soft and elegant, and free from the mundane. The theater has nearly two thousand seats, making it the theater with the most seats for screening domestic films in Shanghai. They have now all been repainted and upholstered with soft cushions and silk covers, making them extremely comfortable.

The light on the screen of the theater, for all old viewers of domestic films, is universally praised. Now, the lamp box components have been replaced, making it even brighter and clearer. The sound section has also been replaced with the latest Ikang sound equipment, which not only has a loud sound but is also very accurate, with little difference from the original sound. The screen is not only made of rubber but is also of a size that other cinemas cannot match.

A Scene from "Women's Rights"

The film "Women's Rights" is the most important production of the Star Film Company this year and is Hu Die's first masterpiece after her marriage. It tells the story of an intellectual woman struggling in an adverse environment, which is both commendable and tearful, and extraordinary. It is directed by Zhang Shichuan and written by Hong Shen. From the opening to the closing, Hu Die appears in almost every scene, which is even more rare.

Following "Women's Rights," the New China Film Company's "Flowers of Revelry," adapted by Mr. Shi Dongshan from "The Government Inspector," will be shown in the theater. This is also a surprising harvest in the domestic film scene this year. In addition, there is also "Little Lingzi," directed by Peng Buga and starring Tan Ying. The success of this film exceeded our expectations. Perhaps no one who has seen the preview does not praise it.

In short, the owner of Jin Cheng is determined to build the theater into the most upscale and magnificent theater and to make it the most satisfactory entertainment venue for Chinese people. Therefore, not only are efforts made to achieve excellence in equipment, but also in various aspects of management, and efforts are made to innovate.

News from Minxin Film Production

The first production of Minxin Company, "Maternal Love," written and directed by Jin Qingyu, is a full-sound dialogue film, co-starring Lin Chuchu, Li Keng, Ge Zuozhi, Hu Yixing, Zhao Hua, Song Xiaodie, Hong Ling, Huang Yunzhen, Zhi Zhihua, Fei Boqing, Wen Rong, etc. It has now been fully completed, and the results are extraordinarily satisfactory. It will soon be premiered at the Jin Cheng Grand Theater in Shanghai.

The famous screenwriter Zhong Shigen, author of "Humanity," "City Night," "Life," and "Family Ethics," will soon direct his new work "The Gate of Spirit and Flesh" himself, and will be co-directed by Zhao Ce. The script has already been sent to Beijing for review and will be filmed as soon as it passes, as the second production of Minxin Company.

The script for Minxin's "Third Production" has long been decided and is currently being actively prepared. As soon as the script passes, it may be filmed at the same time as "The Gate of Spirit and Flesh." At that time, there will be an unprecedented grand occasion on the set of Minxin. It is expected that the two films can be completed simultaneously at the latest within the year.

Following the procedures for the third production, the fourth production is a new work directed by Jin Qingyu, and the fifth production is another script written by Zhong Shigen. As for the script and director candidates for the productions after this, negotiations are still in progress and have not yet been announced.

The "Special Issue of Maternal Love" has now been published, and the content is quite substantial. The whole book has a total of thirty-two pages, with copper plates occupying twelve pages. The text includes "Words from the Director," "Anecdotes and Interesting Stories Magazine," "Suzhou Trip," "Minxin Magazine Work Diary," etc. Each copy is sold for only five cents.
